Your reasoning doesn't."; (04) [KahnemanKleinSynthesis](src/components/marketing/KahnemanKleinSynthesis.tsx) — the IP moat beat: the only platform combining Kahneman's debiasing with Klein's Recognition-Primed Decision framework in one pipeline (biasDetective + noiseJudge + statisticalJury on Kahneman's side, rpdRecognition + forgottenQuestions + pre-mortem on Klein's side, arbitrated by metaJudge). Two-column layout: copy left + convergent cluster viz right. This is the slide-2 pitch-deck claim — no competitor (Cloverpop, Palantir, IBM Watson) combines both traditions. Do NOT dilute this beat with feature copy; keep it framework-first; (05) [MomentsPyramid](src/components/marketing/MomentsPyramid.tsx) — Pyramid-style vertical alternating panels, **five moments** each with a bespoke SVG illustration in [src/components/marketing/moments/](src/components/marketing/moments/): (01) DecisionGraphViz (rich layered temporal graph: 3 quarter-rings, mixed decision/bias/outcome node shapes, live +1 Q4 node), (02) BoardroomViz, (03) AuditTraceViz, (04) DqiGaugeViz (counterfactual / what-if), (05) OutcomeLoopViz (Brier calibration + loop-closure); (06) What-we-replace before/after card (inline, unchanged); (07) Security beat — [SecurityLifecycleStrip](src/components/marketing/SecurityLifecycleStrip.tsx) dynamic 4-stage animated flow sitting ABOVE the refactored CredibilityTrio cards; (08) Proof via [CaseStudyCarousel](src/components/marketing/CaseStudyCarousel.tsx); (09) Close — FAQ + CompetitorComparison → final CTA + Newsletter → Footer. **Pricing is NOT on the landing** (cut 2026-04-21 — reads as desperate; live on `/pricing` only; nav + footer + final CTA link there). **Floating overlay:** [ScrollRevealGraph](src/components/marketing/ScrollRevealGraph.tsx) — 320×320 bottom-right panel on desktop ≥1024px. **Rewritten 2026-04-22 (third pass, final) from a live-audit mockup to an "anatomy of a call" capability constellation:** the live-audit version read as a cheap dashboard mockup and sat on top of the competitor-comparison / FAQ beats. Replaced with an ambient, abstract visualization — a central green "DI" core glyph with five rigor-layer tiles (Graph, Boardroom, Audit, What-if, Outcome) arranged in a pentagon around it. As the reader scrolls, each tile lights up and threads an edge inward; ambient pulse particles flow from each active node toward the core; once all five are active the core ring pulses slowly and the caption reads "EVERY ANGLE · ONE CALL". Eyebrow label: `Decision Intel · anatomy of a call`. Subtitle cycles through the active capability's full name. 6 stages: `STAGE_THRESHOLDS = [0, 0.08, 0.18, 0.28, 0.4, 0.55]`: (0) quiet core only; (1) Knowledge Graph activates; (2) Boardroom; (3) Reasoning audit; (4) What-if; (5) Outcome loop — fully composed. **Visibility range narrowed to `0.04 < scrollProgress < 0.72`** so the overlay fades out before the competitor comparison, FAQ, and final CTA block — no more overlap with actionable content. Dismissible, click-to-expand modal still shows the full 3D [HeroDecisionGraph](src/components/marketing/HeroDecisionGraph.tsx) (WeWork S-1 sample). Respects `prefers-reduced-motion`. Mobile/tablet: hidden. **Live-audit / portfolio-preview / abstract-node variants all retired** — the constellation is the final form. **Palette progression:** white → navy (02) → white (03) → slate-50 (04 synthesis) → slate/white alternation (05, 5 panels) → slate-50 (06) → navy (07) → white (08) → slate-50/navy (close). **Cut from landing:** inline 4-chip trust strip, [CategoryGapShowcase](src/components/marketing/CategoryGapShowcase.tsx) usage, inline HeroDecisionGraph embed, inline pricing section + `handleCheckout`. **Still banned:** Stats bar, PipelineLandingTeaser, OutcomeDetectionViz, Features cards, mid-page BookDemoCTA, startup voice, `agent`/`LangGraph`/`12-node`/`3 independent AI judges` language outside `/how-it-works`. Hero H1 + subhead remain canon.
- **`/demo` route — actual location is `src/app/demo/page.tsx` (NOT under the `(marketing)` route group).** This is a 2,800-line client component that already does paste-first flow with [PasteAuditResults](src/components/marketing/demo/PasteAuditResults.tsx), [scanForPii](src/lib/utils/redaction-scanner.ts), [RedactionPreModal](src/components/ui/RedactionPreModal.tsx), the existing sample picker, and the deep-dive `/demo/[slug]` cards. The 2026-04-25 P0 audit claimed `/demo` 404s because the auditor only checked `src/app/(marketing)/demo/` (which only contains `[slug]/`). The flat `src/app/demo/` directory was missed — `/demo` has been live the whole time. **Do NOT create `src/app/(marketing)/demo/page.tsx`** — Next.js treats route groups as transparent for URL resolution, so `/(marketing)/demo` and `/demo` both resolve to the same `/demo` URL and the build fails with "two parallel pages." This trap was hit twice (2026-04-25 morning P0 restore + the same morning's deploy after CI fixes). When working on `/demo` improvements, edit the existing client component at `src/app/demo/page.tsx` directly. The famous-decision deep-view route at `src/app/(marketing)/demo/[slug]/page.tsx` is untouched and stays. **`/api/demo/run` is SSE-streamed (locked 2026-05-17 — core-flow friction audit #1).** It mirrors `/api/analyze/stream`: same `analyzeDocument(documentId, onProgress)` (zero change to the audit or persistence — only the transport), `formatSSE` + `formatSSEHeartbeat`, terminal `type:'complete'` event carrying `{ documentId, analysisId, result }`, `type:'error'` carrying the message. The client (`demo/page.tsx runPasteAudit`) consumes it with the shared `SSEReader` and drives `pasteStageIdx` from the **real** `progress` number. **Never reintroduce a decoupled progress timer** — the prior fake `setInterval` cycler (every 5500ms, capped) could visibly desync from the real pipeline on the highest-leverage acquisition surface (a stranger pasting a memo); the SSE stream is the single source of truth. Pre-stream guards (env 503 / IP+global rate-limit 429 / word 400/413) still return JSON before the stream opens — the client checks `!res.ok` first, then reads the stream.

- **Marketing copy discipline — no named-prospect leaks (locked 2026-04-25, hardened 2026-04-26):** This is the single most important discipline rule on marketing surfaces. **Never** ship a public route, page title, JSON-LD entry, metadata description, visible HTML copy, OR any source-code comment in a shipped client bundle that names a specific prospect or design-partner ("Sankore", "Wiz", any other firm we have not closed publicly), or any "{firm}-class buyers" coding pattern. Three real catches in the 2026-04-25 + 2026-04-26 audits: `security/page.tsx:464` rendered "Sankore-class buyers" in the hero subhead; `WelcomeModal.tsx:28-31` carried a "Sankore is the design partner" comment that ships in the production bundle; and the persona-audit's recommended "promote the Sankore brief to a public `/sankore` page" was queued before the founder caught it. The right delivery shape for a prospect-specific brief is a private channel (PDF email, token-gated link with `noindex`, in-call screen-share) or a generic page that doesn't name the prospect (e.g. `/for-funds`). Comments must be role-neutral — say "the fund/investor persona identified in design-partner research", not the prospect name. The brief in [src/components/founder-hub/sankore/](src/components/founder-hub/sankore/) stays inside the founder hub. When a future audit recommends building a public page named after any prospect, evaluate against this rule first — the persona is recommending a need, not a delivery shape.
- **DPR architecture lock — McKinsey-grade rebuild (locked 2026-05-05, ALL FOUR PHASES SHIPPED):** the production DPR is being rebuilt as a McKinsey-grade procurement deliverable. Prior generator at [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) (1,696 LOC jsPDF) is dev-grade typography; the legacy sample script at [scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs](scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs) (1,069 LOC) is the same. Both will be retired in Phase 4. **Architecture decisions (locked):** (1) **Rendering tech: HTML/CSS via Next.js route** at [/dpr-render/[type]/[id]](src/app/dpr-render/[type]/[id]/page.tsx) + Tailwind 4 + Inter (body) + Source Serif 4 (display) + JetBrains Mono (hashes), all loaded via @fontsource (local, GDPR-safe). Server PDF generation via puppeteer-core + @sparticuz/chromium-min at [/api/dpr/render-pdf](src/app/api/dpr/render-pdf/route.ts) (Vercel-compatible, ~50MB chromium binary downloaded at first invocation). Client-side export via window.print() after opening the route in a new tab. Build-time sample PDFs via full puppeteer in a script (Phase 4). NOT react-pdf (typography ceiling lower, slow iteration loop, no Tailwind reuse). NOT jsPDF (current; insufficient quality). **Why HTML/CSS wins**: the browser is the most powerful typography engine ever built; CSS hot-reload makes iteration 10× faster than re-rendering PDFs; reuses existing Tailwind / shadcn / Lucide / Inter from the project. Cold start cost ~1-3s on Vercel; warm ~300ms. Memory rule saved: `feedback-best-not-simplest` — choose the best option for the use case, not the simplest infrastructure. (2) **Page architecture: LEGAL-EVIDENCE-RECORD STYLE, not McKinsey-deck.** Per master KB synthesis (NotebookLM 2026-05-05): "Executive buyers and procurement gatekeepers do not want to see the AI's opinion first; they want to see the cryptographic and methodological provenance that proves the document's legal defensibility." Page order locked: (page 1) cover + cryptographic integrity (record-id, hashes, schema version, audit timestamp, verification block) — Phase 1 SHIPPED; (page 2) methodological defensibility (judge variance / noise stats / model lineage / prompt fingerprint) — Phase 2; (page 3) R²F procurement strips (Validity / Reference Class / Feedback Adequacy / Org Calibration / Counterfactual Impact) — Phase 2; (pages 4-N) per-bias finding cards with severity meter (5-segment) + verbatim evidence quote + **"Harden with:" audit-committee-ready hardening question** + regulatory mapping + mitigation — Phase 3; (page N+1) Structural Assumptions Dalio cards — Phase 3; (page N+2) Regulatory Crosswalk grid (19-framework registry across G7/EU/GCC/African markets) — Phase 3; (page N+3) Reviewer Decisions HITL log — Phase 4 retro-fit; (page N+4) Package/deal members — Phase 4; (page N+5) Data Lifecycle footer — Phase 4. (3) **Color palette: severity-led, Kahneman-grade contrast.** Per Kahneman: "If you use color, you are more likely to be believed if your text is printed in bright blue or red than in middling shades of green, yellow, or pale blue." Bright red (#dc2626) for critical, bright blue (#2563eb) for high (Kahneman optimum), amber (#d97706) for medium, restrained green for low/positive only. Navy 900 (#0a0e27) brand band stays as anchor; warm grey 100-950 for hierarchy. DI green DEMOTED from decoration to severity-low only. (4) **Typography pairing**: Inter Variable body + Source Serif 4 Variable display (free, @fontsource) + JetBrains Mono Variable for hashes. High-contrast Kahneman-grade legibility on every text run. Tokens locked in [src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css](src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css). (5) **Per-finding card structure (locked)**: severity meter (5-segment horizontal bar) + verbatim evidence quote + "Harden with:" hardening question (template library indexed by bias type, NOT LLM-generated per-call) + regulatory mapping + mitigation suggestion. (6) **Vocabulary discipline (cross-confirmed)**: "tamper-evident today, private-key signing on Q3 2026 roadmap" — never "signed"; "aligned with AI Verify" — never "certified"; "SOC 2 Type II infrastructure" — never "SOC 2 certified"; replace cold "Brier 0.258" with "143-case reference-class corpus from primary sources". META-RULE: "honest disclosures are a procurement weapon — overclaims destroy trust." **Shipped state (Phase 4 ship 2026-05-05):** **15 physical pages** of McKinsey-grade typography rendering on `/dpr-render/[type]/[id]`. Phase 1 = page 1 cover + cryptographic integrity. Phase 2 = page 2 methodological defensibility (judge variance + model lineage) + page 3 R²F procurement strips (5 strips: Validity / Reference Class / Feedback Adequacy / Org Calibration / Counterfactual Impact). Phase 3 = page 4 per-bias finding cards (severity meter + verbatim evidence + Harden-with hardening question + regulatory mapping + mitigation) + page 5 Dalio Structural Assumptions + page 6 19-framework Regulatory Crosswalk grid by region. Phase 4 = wire-in across all consumers + retired legacy + Dangote specimen. **Active surfaces (all 6 consumers wired)**: `/api/public/sample-dpr` (Phase 2 swap, public specimen, rate-limited 10/hr/IP) · `/api/documents/[id]/provenance-record?format=pdf` (Phase 4, Pro-plan-gated, audit-logged, external-share notification preserved) · `/api/decision-packages/[id]/provenance-record?format=pdf` (Phase 4) · `/api/deals/[id]/provenance-record?format=pdf` (Phase 4) · `/api/compliance/audit-packet/[analysisId]` (Phase 4, legacy URL kept stable) · `/documents/[id]` Export DPR button (Phase 4, blob-URL download). All 6 consumers go through the shared `renderDprPdf()` helper at [src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts](src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts), forwarding the caller's Supabase auth cookie to the headless Chromium so `/dpr-render/document|package|deal/[id]` re-verifies ownership server-side as defense-in-depth. **Specimens**: `/dpr-render/specimen/wework` (canonical S-1 retro, Project Heliograph DACH narrative) + `/dpr-render/specimen/dangote` (Pan-African industrial expansion narrative, locked 2026-05-05 P4 #4). Both regenerate `public/dpr-sample-{wework,dangote}.pdf` via `node scripts/dev-dpr-preview.mjs` against the running dev server. **Data flow**: `assembleProvenanceRecordData` (+ Package + Deal variants) now populates `findingsAugment: Record<biasType, { evidenceQuote, mitigation, severityOverride, confidenceOverride }>` from `analysis.biases` (excerpt + suggestion + severity + confidence). The /dpr-render route reads `data.findingsAugment` for real audits, falls back to `SAMPLE_FINDINGS_AUGMENT` / `DANGOTE_FINDINGS_AUGMENT` for specimens. Single deriver path: `deriveDprFindings(data, augment)` joins citations + regulatoryMapping + counterfactualImpact + the hardening-question template library at [src/lib/reports/dpr-hardening-questions.ts](src/lib/reports/dpr-hardening-questions.ts) (15 canonical bias→hardening-question mappings, indexed by bias type, NOT LLM-generated per audit). **Client-Safe Export Mode**: `?clientSafe=1` query param flows from API consumer → `/dpr-render` route → classification chip flips to "Client-safe export" + redaction logic engages (entity / amount / person-name placeholders for the meta strip + summary; redaction within finding cards is a follow-up since the per-bias evidence quotes already get authored under the no-named-prospects discipline). **Legacy retirement**: the 1,696-LOC `decision-provenance-record-generator.ts` (jsPDF) is no longer called by any active code path — only doc / comment references remain. The 1,069-LOC `scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs` no longer generates DPR samples (only DPA template + DOCX); the buildDprSample + buildDprDangote functions are retained as emergency fallback but commented out of the run path. **Forward-looking rule**: when any visual / typography / color / layout decision changes, update [src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css](src/app/dpr-render/dpr.css) only — every page component reads from these CSS-variable tokens. When a new consumer surface needs a DPR PDF, import `renderDprPdf` from [src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts](src/lib/reports/render-dpr-pdf.ts) — never re-import the legacy jsPDF generator.

- **Trust-copy single source of truth (locked 2026-04-26, extended 2026-05-01):** [src/lib/constants/trust-copy.ts](src/lib/constants/trust-copy.ts) is the canonical home for procurement-stage security claims that appear on multiple marketing surfaces. - **DPR vocabulary lock — "hashed + tamper-evident", NOT "signed + hashed" (locked 2026-04-26):** the 2026-04-26 persona audit (James + Margaret) caught "signed, hashed" overclaim across 16 surfaces. The implementation in [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) produces SHA-256 input hashes; it does NOT cryptographically sign with a Decision Intel private key. Until private-key signing ships, every consumer must describe the artefact as "hashed + tamper-evident" — see `DPR_PROVENANCE_*` constants. When private-key signing ships, restore "signed" by updating the constants in `trust-copy.ts` and the explanatory header in `provenance-record-data.ts`.

Wired into [MarketingNav](src/components/marketing/MarketingNav.tsx) (Enterprise mega-menu), the landing-page footer, and [sitemap.ts](src/app/sitemap.ts).
- **Privacy-policy GDPR Art 13 mandatory disclosures (added 2026-04-26):** [/privacy](<src/app/(marketing)/privacy/page.tsx>) carries the four disclosures GDPR Art 13 requires: (1) Controller identity block — pulls from `company-info.ts`; (2) Lawful Basis section — `LAWFUL_BASIS` array maps each processing activity to its Art 6 basis; (3) Right to lodge a supervisory complaint (Art 77) — bottom of the Rights section, links to ICO / CNIL / Irish DPC / Nigerian NITDA / SA Information Regulator; (4) International Transfers section — names DPF, SCCs, IDTA, NDPR-transfer agreements, PoPIA s.72. The processors list also gained `Resend` and `Cloudflare` (sub-processors James caught as missing under Art 28(3)(d)). When adding a new processing activity (new product feature, new analytics path, new sub-processor), update LAWFUL_BASIS + PROCESSORS in the same commit so the privacy page never drifts from the actual data flows. Also: GDPR rights array gained an Art 22 automated-decision-contestation card.
- **Cross-reference auto-trigger 30-min cooldown (parity, 2026-04-26):** [/api/analyze/stream](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) auto-fires a deal cross-reference when an analysis completes on a deal with ≥2 analyzed docs. The 2026-04-26 audit caught the deal-side missing the package-side's 30-min cooldown — meaning back-to-back uploads could fire N runs at ~£0.40 Gemini cost each. Both deal + package now check `dealCrossReference.findFirst({ runAt: { gt: now - 30min } })` before firing. The manual button on the deal page bypasses the cooldown via its own per-user 20/hr rate limit. **Note**: Marcus's 2026-04-26 audit incorrectly claimed cross-reference was manual-only — the auto-trigger has shipped since 3.1 deep. CLAUDE.md was right; the audit was wrong (verification miss on the analyze/stream route). Always grep the route before claiming a feature is missing.
- **EU/Multi-region quote builder honesty (locked 2026-04-26):** the public + admin EnterpriseQuoteBuilder UI still offers `US`, `EU`, and `Multi-region`. Production today runs Vercel + Supabase US. When the user picks EU or Multi-region, an inline amber-tinted disclaimer surfaces in the form and the rendered PDF (a) labels the Region row as "EU (Enterprise-conversation residency, not production today)" and (b) appends a short italic note in the contracted-artefacts section explaining what the picked preference actually means. The server-side coercion to `US` was REMOVED — the user's pick is honoured in the PDF, with the disclaimer making it impossible for a procurement reader to interpret it as a current-state guarantee. Until EU residency is actually provisioned, leave both layers (UI inline disclaimer + PDF clarifying note) intact.
- **Document-detail mobile (locked 2026-04-26):** the [/documents/[id]](<src/app/(platform)/documents/[id]/page.tsx>) main grid (`gridTemplateColumns: '1fr 380px'`) and the tab bar (`flex-wrap + overflow:hidden`) BOTH had no mobile breakpoint. On phones the sidebar column crushed the main content and the tab bar silently clipped the second row of tabs. Fix shipped 2026-04-26: classes `doc-detail-main-grid` + `doc-detail-tab-bar` plus a scoped `<style>` block at the bottom of the page with a `@media (max-width: 900px)` rule that stacks the grid to a single column and switches the tab bar to horizontal scroll. **Don't add new top-level inline styles** that override these classes on the same elements without also adding a matching mobile override; the `<style>` block is the single mobile override and has to win on the narrow viewport.

Native browser dialogs break the modal stack on Safari mobile, disrupt screen-readers, and read as 2008-vintage during procurement-stage demos. - **DPA DOCX redline-ready format (locked 2026-05-01, James persona ask):** [scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs](scripts/generate-legal-pdfs.mjs) now emits BOTH `public/dpa-template.pdf` (read-only procurement reference) AND `public/dpa-template.docx` (Word-native, redline-ready) from the same body content. F500 GC redline workflows expect DOCX with Track Changes; the PDF version stayed because procurement-led intake teams expect a read-only reference alongside. The DOCX is a hand-built minimal Office Open XML zip (5 parts: `[Content_Types].xml`, `_rels/.rels`, `word/document.xml`, `word/styles.xml`, `word/numbering.xml`, `word/_rels/document.xml.rels`) using `jszip` already in the dependency tree — no new packages. Body content is mirror-image of the PDF version section-for-section so a procurement reader compares without surprise. Both surface as side-by-side download CTAs at the bottom of [security/page.tsx](<src/app/(marketing)/security/page.tsx>) — "DPA template · PDF" + "DPA template · DOCX". When the DPA changes, edit the body strings in `buildDpaDocx()` and `buildDpaTemplate()` in lockstep — the format-divergence between the two artefacts is the bug class.

- **Education Room — flashcard + recall + apply mastery engine (locked 2026-04-28):** [EducationRoomTab](src/components/founder-hub/EducationRoomTab.tsx) is the founder-hub's recollection engine. Reading Closing Lab + Sales Toolkit + founder-context builds familiarity; recollection under pressure builds the muscle that fires in a live conversation. **Three modes per deck**: Flashcard (passive recall — see prompt, click to flip, self-grade missed/almost/got-it; SM-2 spaced repetition tracks card mastery over time), Recall (active recall — type the answer in your own voice, gemini-3.1-flash-lite grades semantically against canonical, returns score 0-100 + grade letter + what landed + what missed + coach note + canonical reveal), Apply (scenario application drill — see prompt + a concrete scenario context like "you're on a procurement call with a GC", type how you'd USE the concept, AI grades application quality). **SSOT** at [education-room-data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/education/education-room-data.ts) — 15 decks × 161 cards as of 2026-05-02 (was 12 decks × ~100 at the 2026-04-28 lock; expanded with `advanced_sales_moves`, `strategic_thinking`, `goldner_discovery` decks per the Brinkmanship + Strategic Thinking + Goldner Discovery additions): DI Vocabulary (20 cards — locked + banned + cold-context bridges + numbers like 135 decisions / 17 frameworks / ~90% margin / per-audit cost / specimen library / first design partner Sankore-marked-confidential), Buyer Personas (14 cards — basics + verbatim opener + canonical objection-handler response per persona), Maalouf 6 Principles, Satyam 5 Pillars, Silent Objections (5 — each with current ship status: shipped / in-progress / todo so the founder always sees the gap), Sales DQI Rubric (11 dimensions — one card per dimension with excellent/poor + weight), Cognitive Biases (10 most common in strategic memos — confirmation, anchoring, sunk-cost, narrative fallacy, overconfidence, availability, halo effect, illusion of control, planning fallacy, loss aversion as both bias-to-defend AND sales-tool), 12-Node Pipeline (6 representative — structuralAssumptions, biasDetective, noiseJudge, rpdRecognition, pre-mortem, metaJudge), DQI Methodology (5 — components+weights, grade boundaries 85/70/55/40, Brier score, recalibration, validation), 17 Regulatory Frameworks (8 most invoked — EU AI Act Art 14, Basel III ICAAP, GDPR Art 22, NDPR, CBN, WAEMU, PoPIA s.71, ISA 2007 with current TODO-gap callout), R²F Framework (5 — Kahneman side / Klein side / metaJudge arbitration / 2009 anchor paper / competitor gap), Founder One-Liners (8 — External Attack Vectors, ICP wedge vs ceiling, generic-VC-segment-to-avoid, primary one-liner, secondary regulatory variant, protected-revenue framing, outcome-gate strategic purpose, design-partner contractual asks). **Each card** carries: stable id slug (used as localStorage key for SM-2 state), prompt, canonicalAnswer (ground truth for AI grading), optional hint, difficulty (foundation/core/advanced), applicationContext (when this comes up in real conversation — used as apply-mode scenario), source citation, optional category tag. **SM-2 spaced repetition lite** in `applySm2()` helper — tracks easeFactor / repetitions / intervalDays / lastReviewed / nextDue / totalReviews / successfulReviews per card; cards graded "missed" come up sooner, "got it" cards push out exponentially. Deck picker shows per-deck mastery (% of cards with ≥2 successful reviews) + due-card count. **API endpoint**: [/api/founder-hub/education/grade-recall](src/app/api/founder-hub/education/grade-recall/route.ts) uses gemini-3.1-flash-lite (cheap, classification-grade) at temperature 0.3 for recall grading consistency; mock fallback when GOOGLE_API_KEY missing. Founder-pass auth. **Persistence**: localStorage `di-education-room-sm2-v1` (per-card SM-2 state), `di-education-room-session-v1` (lifetime reviewed/got-it/almost/missed counts). **Per-card recall cost**: ~£0.005-0.015 (one cheap Gemini call per recall submission). **When to use**: morning before a London networking event (drill the persona-opener deck for whoever you'll meet), after every CLAUDE.md positioning lock change (the relevant cards inherit the new vocab — re-drill them), before any procurement-stage call (drill the regulatory-frameworks deck). Tab id `education_room` registered in Go-to-Market group between Closing Lab and Sparring Room — the read→recall→do flow. **Forward-looking rule**: when CLAUDE.md positioning vocabulary changes, update the relevant card.canonicalAnswer in education-room-data.ts in the same commit. When a new persona / framework / lesson lands, add a card. The founder is the only consumer; cards are written in HIS voice for HIS recall — not generic SaaS marketing copy. Pattern lifted from [Nexus Tracker](https://github.com/FolahanWilliams/nexus-tracker) MindForge (vocab + summary + impromptu-speaking modules with SM-2 spaced repetition), extended for DI's specific knowledge surface.
- **Brinkmanship + Strategic Thinking (locked 2026-04-28 PM):** Two new sections in [SalesToolkitTab](src/components/founder-hub/SalesToolkitTab.tsx) sourcing from Schelling "The Strategy of Conflict" (1960) + Dixit & Nalebuff "Thinking Strategically" (1991). **Brinkmanship section** — 4 game-theory moves that flip the power dynamic by deliberately creating the risk of a mutually-bad outcome (the deal dying): Evidence-Moment ultimatum · weaponized honest off-ramp · reject the unpaid dev shop · natural scarcity on pilot seats. Each carries verbatim phrase + mechanism + anti-pattern + which Sparring dimension it scores against + best-for-persona. Stored as `BRINKMANSHIP_MOVES: SalesMove[]` in [sales-toolkit.ts](src/lib/data/sales-toolkit.ts). **Strategic Thinking Principles** — 5 higher-order positioning anchors that govern HOW DI is built, sold, and positioned (look-forward-reason-backward, strategic moves by limiting options, credible commitments, setting category ground rules, cooperation/coordination over competition). Stored as `STRATEGIC_THINKING_PRINCIPLES: StrategicPrinciple[]` with `principle / summary / diApplication / whenItBites` fields. Rendered via new `StrategicPrinciplesList` component at the bottom of SalesToolkitTab. **Education Room extensions**: 4 brinkmanship cards added to `advanced_sales_moves` deck + new `strategic_thinking` deck (5 cards × principles). **Sparring grade prompt awareness**: brinkmanship is now named as the META-PATTERN that fires when `mutual_disqualification + pressure_without_pressure + damaging_admission` cluster high (4-5) together. The grader is instructed to call it out in the strengths array as "brinkmanship signal · power dynamic flipped" with the specific transcript phrase, and to flag the inverse (founder agreeing to every feature request, hedging, chasing the deal) as a recurring pattern when it shows in `recentDimensionAverages`. **Why brinkmanship is NOT a 16th dimension**: it's the meta-pattern that emerges from existing dimensions clustering — adding it as its own dimension would double-count. Treating it as a meta-signal preserves the rubric's parsimony while still surfacing the highest-leverage sales psychology move. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new sales-toolkit moves, treat the existing 15 dimensions as the canonical grading surface; if a new "framework" doesn't decompose into those, don't add it as a dimension — surface it as a SalesMove and let it score against existing dimensions. The grade prompt should be the only place where meta-patterns (like brinkmanship) are named.
- **EducationRoomTab purity + static-component fixes (locked 2026-04-28 PM):** Two ESLint react-hooks rules were tripping CI on the Education Room: (a) `react-hooks/purity` flagged `Date.now()` inside the `deckMastery` useMemo (computing due-card counts) — fix: hoist to a `useState(() => Date.now())` mountTime, capture once, depend the useMemo on the captured value. Minute-level precision is enough for due-card counting; we don't refresh as the user sits on the page. (b) `react-hooks/static-components` flagged the `const Icon = getIcon(...)` pattern in DeckPicker + CardHeader because the resolved component reference would change shape on each render. Fix: declare a module-scoped `<DeckIcon name=... size=... style=... />` component that handles the lookup internally; both call sites now render `<DeckIcon ... />` instead of resolving an icon-component reference inline. Pattern: any `getIcon`-style helper that returns a component constructor needs to be wrapped in a module-scope component to satisfy the static-components rule.
- **Sparring Room v3 (locked 2026-04-28 PM — coach-not-judge upgrade + 4 new dimensions + DQI uptrend visualisation):** Major iteration on the original Sparring Room. (1) **15-dimension rubric** — added `fomu_calibration` (JOLT Effect / Matt Dixon), `damaging_admission` (Cialdini + Cohen Naked Business), `mutual_disqualification` (Sandler), `prescriptive_recommendation` (JOLT) per NotebookLM synthesis on "what failure modes is the rubric NOT catching" (KB note 0cc18c5d). Weights rebalanced to sum to 1.0 across 15 dims. (2) **Coach-not-judge result schema** — every grading response now includes `nextSessionFocus` (2-3 dimensions to laser on next rep, with whyItMatters + concreteAction), `drillPlan` (2-4 ordered concrete actions before next rep, each pointing at a specific Founder Hub surface like "Education Room → Buyer Personas deck → Adaeze cards" with estimatedMinutes), `confidenceBuild` (1-2 sentences naming what GENUINELY worked — not generic praise), `nextRepSetup` (recommendedPersonaId + recommendedMode + rationale based on this rep's score: ≥80 = harder, 60-79 = same persona × different mode, <60 = same persona × easier mode), and conditionally `patternFlag` (only fires at 3+ reps when a recurring weakness shows in `recentDimensionAverages` — pattern + rootCause + breakthroughMove). The grade route now accepts `recentDimensionAverages` (last-5 rolling per-dimension averages from history) + `totalRepsCompleted` and feeds them to the prompt for longitudinal coaching. (3) **DQI uptrend viz** — new [SparringTrendViz](src/components/founder-hub/sparring/SparringTrendViz.tsx) component renders 3 panels: line chart (DQI per rep + 5-rep rolling average + grade-band markers + best-rep callout), per-dimension trend bars (sorted by lift first-5-vs-last-5, source-color coded), and persona×mode performance heatmap (avg DQI per cell with rep count). Pure SVG, respects prefers-reduced-motion. (4) **HistoryEntry shape extended** to v2 capturing `dimensions: Record<GradingDimensionId, number>` + `fillerCount` per rep so the viz has real data; v1 entries (no dimensions) still load gracefully. **Original Sparring Room features preserved**: 7 buyer personas, 7 scenario modes (incl. networking-event-in-person), Wispr Flow paste-transcript flow, mock fallback. **Pattern detection unlocks at 3+ reps** to avoid noisy single-rep flagging. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding a new grading dimension, update GRADING_DIMENSIONS array + GradingDimensionId union + grade prompt's dimensions block + grade prompt's required JSON output template + mock fallback dims object — all in same commit. The weights MUST sum to 1.0 (verify by hand; runtime panic disabled). The earlier 2026-04-28 lock (networking-event mode + Kahneman loss-aversion) stays — this v3 entry supersedes the prior coverage of result-schema + UI sections.
- **Sparring Room — live sales-rep practice (locked 2026-04-28, SUPERSEDED by Sparring Room v3 entry above which lifted the rubric to 15 dimensions; this v1 entry retained for historical context only):** [SparringRoomTab](src/components/founder-hub/SparringRoomTab.tsx) is the founder-hub's reading→doing transition. Closing Lab gives the verbatim phrases per persona; Sparring Room makes you LIVE them under pressure. Workflow: pick buyer persona × scenario mode → AI generates 3 buyer-voice questions in their authentic voice + an opener line → 5-second prep countdown → user records voice answer via Wispr Flow externally (NO in-app transcription — Wispr Flow handles voice→text system-wide) → pastes transcript → AI grades on an 11-dimension Sales DQI rubric (Maalouf 4 + Satyam 3 + DI discipline 2 + Kahneman 1 loss-aversion-framing + fundamentals 1) → returns score + 2 strengths + 3 framework-grounded improvements with verbatim phrases the founder can rehearse + a buyer-perspective simulation showing what the buyer is internally thinking right after the speech. **Architecture**: SSOT at [sparring-room-data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/sparring/sparring-room-data.ts) — 7 buyer personas (Adaeze mid-market PE / Potomac boutique sell-side M&A / Marcus solo fractional CSO + Margaret F500 CSO / Titi Pan-African fund partner / James GC + Riya pre-seed VC), **7 scenario modes** including the new `networking_event_inperson` mode (London networking events — 30-60 second connect-not-pitch with the buyer holding a drink, pre-loaded scenario templates for Margaret-class CSO / Potomac-class M&A head / Titi-class fund partner / Marcus-class fractional CSO / Riya-class VC associate at networking mixers), 11 grading dimensions with explicit excellent/poor descriptions + weights summing to 1.0, 27 scenario templates pairing personas with modes for AI generation hints, plus mechanical analysis utilities. **Loss-aversion framing dimension (Kahneman source, weight 0.10)**: grounded in Kahneman & Tversky 1979 prospect theory — losses weight ~2-2.5× gains in decision-making. Excellent: frames value as preventing a SPECIFIC, named loss the buyer is already worrying about (regrettable strategic mistake, McKinsey bill, LP pulling capital), anchored against a comparable cost. Poor: frames as upside / gain only ('better decisions', 'improved quality') — buyer hears upside and discounts. Weights rebalanced when adding loss-aversion: Maalouf reduced from 4×0.10 to 0.08/0.10/0.10/0.08; Satyam reduced 0.10/0.12/0.08 to 0.08/0.10/0.08; DI discipline reduced vocabulary 0.08→0.06; specificity stays 0.12; new Kahneman 0.10. Sum = 1.00. **Two API endpoints**: [/api/founder-hub/sparring/generate-questions](src/app/api/founder-hub/sparring/generate-questions/route.ts) uses gemini-3-flash-preview at temperature 0.7 to generate persona-voice opener + 3 questions, mock fallback when GOOGLE_API_KEY missing; [/api/founder-hub/sparring/grade](src/app/api/founder-hub/sparring/grade/route.ts) uses gemini-3-flash-preview at temperature 0.4 (lower for grading consistency) returning the full SparringSessionResult schema, plus mechanical filler/banned/locked vocabulary detection that runs WITHOUT calling Gemini. Founder-pass auth on both. **Vocabulary discipline awareness**: the `vocabulary_discipline` dimension downgrades use of locked DI vocabulary (reasoning layer / R²F / DPR / DQI) on COLD-context buyers — the founder picks isWarmContext per session, defaulting to false. The `empathic_mode_first` dimension grades whether the founder led with the BUYER's pain in BUYER's vocabulary BEFORE introducing product. Banned-vocabulary list (decision intelligence platform / decision hygiene / boardroom strategic decision / etc.) auto-detected and surfaced as explicit hit count on results. **Persistence**: localStorage `di-sparring-room-history-v1` tracks recent reps with sales DQI trend (last 5 reps delta + average + per-rep grade letters). **Per-rep cost**: ~£0.05-0.10 (one Gemini call for question generation + one for grading). Heavy use ~3-5 reps/day per session. **When to use**: before any high-stakes meeting (rehearse the persona you're calling), after every lost deal (replay the conversation against the buyer who actually killed it), as muscle-memory training for the Maalouf "authority not trust" + Satyam "conviction transmission" dimensions. Tab id `sparring_room` registered in Go-to-Market group between Closing Lab and Outreach Hub. **Forward-looking rule**: when a new buyer persona archetype emerges from real meetings, add to BUYER_PERSONAS in sparring-room-data.ts in the same commit as any persona-related copy elsewhere (CLAUDE.md ICP, founder-context.ts, role-empty-states). When CLAUDE.md banned/locked vocabulary changes, update DI_BANNED_VOCABULARY and DI_LOCKED_VOCABULARY in sparring-room-data.ts in the same commit. Pattern lifted from [Nexus Tracker](https://github.com/FolahanWilliams/nexus-tracker) MindForge impromptu-speaking module, extended for B2B sales conversations.

- **DPR v2 enhancements (locked 2026-04-26 — schema bumped to v2, six new sections from NotebookLM "highest-ROI DPR additions" synthesis):** the Decision Provenance Record generator at [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) now ships six new procurement-grade blocks alongside the existing 4-page core. Page sequence: (1) cover with Integrity Fingerprints + new **Verification block** (re-verification path, "tamper-evident today, private-key signing on Q3 2026 roadmap" honesty) + new **Org Calibration strip** (Cloverpop defense — proves the DQI is calibrated against THIS org's outcome history, not a generic benchmark) + new **Counterfactual Impact block** (top-3 bias scenarios with expected improvement %, sample-size + Wilson confidence, monetary anchor when DecisionFrame.value is present), (2) model lineage + judge variance, (3) academic citations + 17-framework regulatory mapping, (4) pipeline lineage + appendix, (5) NEW **Reviewer Decisions / HITL log** (accepted mitigations, dismissed flags with reasons, dissent log, final sign-off — EU AI Act Art 14 + Basel III Pillar 2 ICAAP qualitative-decision documentation; only rendered when reviewerDecisions.reviewedAt is non-null), (6) blind-prior aggregations (when present), (7) Decision Package or Deal members (when applicable), (8) NEW **Data Lifecycle footer** ALWAYS as the last page (retention window per plan tier, encryption posture, sub-processors, right-to-erasure, production region, published roadmap items — the procurement-grade contractual statement F500 vendor-risk registers ask for in writing). New top-level field: **Client-Safe Export Mode** (`generate(data, { clientSafe: true })`) — entity names, amounts, and person names in the meta strip + summary + reviewer notes are replaced with stable `[ENTITY_N]` / `[AMOUNT_N]` / `[NAME_N]` placeholders so the artefact can be shared with an LP, regulator, or third-party assurance firm without leaking competitive intelligence. Wired through three API routes via `?clientSafe=1` query param: [/api/documents/[id]/provenance-record](src/app/api/documents/[id]/provenance-record/route.ts), [/api/decision-packages/[id]/provenance-record](src/app/api/decision-packages/[id]/provenance-record/route.ts), [/api/deals/[id]/provenance-record](src/app/api/deals/[id]/provenance-record/route.ts), and the public specimen at [/api/public/sample-dpr](src/app/api/public/sample-dpr/route.ts). The assembler at [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) populates counterfactualImpact (via `computeCounterfactuals(analysisId, orgId)`), orgCalibration (via `getOrgBrierStats(prisma, orgId)` + `Analysis.recalibratedDqi`), and dataLifecycle (always populated, pulls plan-tier retention + sub-processor list + roadmap) — each block is independently fault-tolerant; failure to populate one returns undefined and the PDF skips that section honestly rather than fabricating data. reviewerDecisions stays undefined in the live assembler until the capture UI ships; the SPECIMEN at [sample-dpr.ts](src/lib/reports/sample-dpr.ts) seeds plausible v2 values across all six new sections so a CSO + GC can preview the full v2 shape via `/api/public/sample-dpr?clientSafe=0|1` before signing anything. **Vocabulary discipline**: the cover purpose strap reads "Hashed and tamper-evident evidence record..." — the prior overclaim "signed, hashed" is gone; restore "signed" only when private-key signing actually ships per `trust-copy.ts` lock. **The strategic point**: this DPR v2 is the leave-behind artefact that lands the warm-intro meeting (LRQA / Ian Spaulding, Sankore, future F500 conversations) — it carries (a) Cloverpop-defense (org calibration), (b) IBM-watsonx-defense (HITL log proving humans governed the call), (c) agentic-shift-defense (the artefact maps onto ANY structured decision artefact, not just human-authored memos), and (d) procurement-grade transparency that LRQA-style assurance firms recognise as their own vocabulary.
- **Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint EXTENDED (locked 2026-04-30 — items 6 of 10):** Second batch ships #8 / #2-structural / #9 alongside the first batch's #5 / #3 / #6. The DPR cover page now carries SIX procurement-grade Kahneman-Klein-anchored signals in addition to the existing audit summary: **Validity classification → Org Calibration → Feedback Adequacy → Reference Class Forecast → Counterfactual Impact → Recommended Action**. **(#8 — Reference Class Forecasting · Kahneman & Lovallo 2003 "Delusions of Success" HBR)** New module [reference-class-forecast.ts](src/lib/learning/reference-class-forecast.ts) — pure-function similarity scoring against the 143-case library (no LLM call, deterministic, <5ms). Returns top-5 historical analogs + matched-class baseline failure rate + four-band predicted outcome (succeeds / mixed / struggles / fails / too_small_to_judge). Wired into [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts); rendered as a colour-coded REFERENCE CLASS FORECAST · {BAND} strip on every DPR cover. Specimen seeded with WeWork (2019) as the lead analog. Cold-start posture is honest — structurally novel decisions return `reference_class_too_small_to_judge` rather than a fabricated forecast. **(#2 — Validity Classifier with structural DQI shift · Kahneman & Klein 2009 first condition)** New module [validity-classifier.ts](src/lib/learning/validity-classifier.ts) — `classifyValidity({ documentType, industry, decisionHorizon? })` returns one of four bands (high / medium / low / zero) with a rationale string. `getValidityWeightShift(class)` returns `Partial<WEIGHTS>` deltas applied via [computeEffectiveWeights](src/lib/scoring/dqi.ts) — in low-validity environments: `+0.10 historicalAlignment, +0.02 biasLoad, −0.05 evidenceQuality, −0.04 processMaturity, −0.03 complianceRisk` (re-normalised to sum 1.0). In zero-validity: `+0.20 historicalAlignment, +0.04 biasLoad, −0.08 evidenceQuality, −0.10 processMaturity, −0.06 complianceRisk`. **METHODOLOGY_VERSION bumped 2.0.0 → 2.1.0** (locked 2026-04-30); legacy inputs without `validityClass` still report `'2.0.0-no-validity'` so a procurement reader can tell which methodology produced a given DQI. Wired into all 3 DQI computation paths: [/api/dqi](src/app/api/dqi/route.ts), [/api/v1/dqi](src/app/api/v1/dqi/route.ts), [/api/explainability/[id]](src/app/api/explainability/[analysisId]/route.ts). DPR renders a VALIDITY · {BAND} strip with rationale + methodology version. **(#9 — Inside-View Dominance · DI-B-022 · Kahneman & Lovallo 2003)** New bias entry — the 22nd in the stable taxonomy. Cascade: BiasCategory union + BIAS_CATEGORIES, [bias-education.ts](src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts) DI-B-022 entry with the 1976 Israeli curriculum-writing team as the canonical example, [bias-normalize.ts](src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts) ALIASES ("Inside-View Dominance" / "reference class neglect" / "outside view neglect"), [BIAS_DETECTIVE_PROMPT](src/lib/agents/prompts.ts) taxonomy item #22 detecting "this case is special" / "the comparables don't apply" / projections without grounded comparables, four new compound interactions (+ Planning Fallacy 1.6×, + Overconfidence 1.5×, + Illusion of Validity 1.4×, + Confirmation 1.3×), new toxic combination "Reference-Class Blindness" (Inside-View + Planning Fallacy + Overconfidence — the canonical Kahneman & Lovallo failure pattern). `forgottenQuestions` taxonomy enum lifted 32 → 33. **Education Room** gained four new flashcards (`bias_reference_class_forecasting`, `bias_validity_classifier`, `bias_inside_view_dominance`, plus the three from batch one) — kahneman_klein tag, advanced tier. **Why this matters**: R²F was previously claimed in marketing copy but only partially operationalised. Six DPR cover blocks anchored in Kahneman-Klein-Lovallo papers, with academic citations + DOI references in every bias-education entry, makes the moat citable not just claimable. The next 4 paper applications (`#1` Fractionation of Expertise, `#10` Calibrated Rejection of Subjective Confidence, `#7` Algorithm-aversion Counter-programming, `#4` Improper Linear Models / Decision Rubric) are the remaining ranked queue. **Forward-looking rule**: every new R²F detector lands with academic anchor in `bias-education.ts academicReference` + Education Room flashcard + chat-coaching context entry in the same commit. The methodology version is now the audit signature — bump it for any structural change to weight calculation; never silently change weights.

- **Pipeline persistence + UI surfacing for R²F signals (locked 2026-04-30 — completes the paper-application sprint #2 + #8):** the validity classification is now PERSISTED in the pipeline at audit-completion time (not just live-computed at render). [/api/analyze/stream](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) extends the `judgeOutputs` Json snapshot with `validityClassification` (the full ValidityClassification shape including band + rationale + signals) when each new Analysis row is created. Three downstream surfaces read the persisted band first, with live-compute fallback for legacy analyses: (a) DPR assembler in [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) (DPR cover strip stays in sync with the band the audit was originally scored against); (b) DQI route handlers — [/api/dqi](src/app/api/dqi/route.ts), [/api/v1/dqi](src/app/api/v1/dqi/route.ts), [/api/explainability/[id]](src/app/api/explainability/[analysisId]/route.ts) — read judgeOutputs.validityClassification and pass it to `computeDQI`; (c) live-audit insights endpoint [/api/analysis/[id]/insights](src/app/api/analysis/[id]/insights/route.ts) returns the band with a `validitySource: 'persisted' | 'live'` discriminator so the UI can show provenance ("pipeline-grade" vs "live-computed"). **No schema migration**: the validity classification rides on the existing `Analysis.judgeOutputs` Json column alongside the existing per-judge variance metadata. **UI surface**: new [PaperApplicationsCard](src/components/analysis/PaperApplicationsCard.tsx) renders all three R²F signals (Validity Classification → Reference Class Forecast → Feedback Adequacy) on the document-detail OverviewTab, mounted between RemediationChecklist and RPDPreMortemSuggestionsCard. Reference-class top-3 analogs are clickable links to [/case-studies/{slug}](<src/app/(marketing)/case-studies/[slug]/page.tsx>) so a procurement reader can pivot from the live audit straight to the historical analog. The card mirrors the DPR cover-page strips one-for-one — same colours, same labels, same rationale text — so a buyer who downloads the DPR sees the same content they read on the live audit. **Why this matters**: prior to this lock the validity band on the DPR was computed at PDF-render time and the DQI was computed at scoring time; the two could drift if the documentType changed between scoring and PDF generation. Persisting at audit-completion makes the band immutable for the lifetime of the analysis. The live-audit UI cards close the gap between "audit ran" and "buyer sees the same six R²F blocks the DPR carries" without forcing the DPR PDF download. **Forward-looking rule**: when a new R²F signal ships, follow the same three-tier wire-up — (1) compute + persist in `judgeOutputs` at audit-completion time; (2) DPR + DQI routes read persisted-first with live fallback; (3) UI card on OverviewTab + insights endpoint. Same shape contract every time.

- **Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint (locked 2026-04-30 — items 3 of 10 from the first batch):** Three load-bearing operationalisations of the 2009 "Conditions for Intuitive Expertise: A Failure to Disagree" paper, the canonical R²F citation. Shipped together because they answer three procurement-grade questions a Fortune 500 CSO or Pan-African fund partner should be able to ask of an audit ("does this memo's confidence match its evidence?", "did the pre-mortem actually fire prospective hindsight?", "has the author of this memo had enough closed-loop feedback for their experience claim to be calibrated?"). **(#5 — prospective hindsight)** The pre-mortem prompts at [src/lib/agents/prompts.ts](src/lib/agents/prompts.ts) lines 386, 485, and 1075 (STRATEGIC_ANALYSIS_PROMPT, DEEP_ANALYSIS_SUPER_PROMPT, buildNarrativePreMortemPrompt) now enforce the EXACT Klein & Mitchell 1995 / Mitchell-Russo-Pennington 1989 framing: project ONE YEAR INTO THE FUTURE, the plan was implemented as written, the outcome was a TOTAL DISASTER, write the HISTORY of that disaster in past tense ("the failure began when…", "the warning sign everyone missed was…"). NO conditional voice ("might", "could", "if") — the past-tense fait-accompli framing is the load-bearing instruction. The cognitive science: generating an explanation for an outcome framed as ALREADY OCCURRED produces 25-30% more, and substantially higher-quality, failure-cause insights than asking "what could go wrong?" in conditional voice. **(#3 — illusion of validity, DI-B-021)** New bias entry at [src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts](src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts) DI-B-021. Wired through (a) `BiasCategory` union and `BIAS_CATEGORIES` map in [src/types/index.ts](src/types/index.ts), (b) ALIASES in [src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts](src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts) (so LLM display-name output "Illusion of Validity" / "Illusory Validity" / "Narrative Coherence" / "Confidence by Coherence" all normalize to the canonical key), (c) BIAS_DETECTIVE_PROMPT taxonomy item #21 at `prompts.ts` with rhetorical-certainty signal patterns ("we are certain", "guaranteed", "highly predictable", "clear path to") detected when not backed by external base rates; (d) validity-aware scoring rule (Kahneman & Klein 2009 first condition) — confidence-language penalised harder in low-validity domains (M&A, market entry, long-horizon strategy) than in high-validity ones; (e) four new compound interactions (Illusion of Validity + Overconfidence 1.5×, + Confirmation 1.4×, + Halo 1.3×, + Authority 1.3×); (f) new toxic combination "Coherent Confidence" (Illusion of Validity + Overconfidence + Confirmation/Halo) — the most dangerous pattern in low-validity domains; (g) `forgottenQuestions` taxonomy enum lifted from 31 to 32 biases. **(#6 — feedback adequacy)** New module at [src/lib/learning/feedback-adequacy.ts](src/lib/learning/feedback-adequacy.ts) exporting `getFeedbackAdequacy(prisma, userId, { domainHint })` returning verdict + closedOutcomes + recentClosedOutcomes (18-month window) + daysSinceLastOutcome + meanBrier + domainMatchCount + procurement-grade note. Verdict bands: ≥10 closed outcomes in domain in past 18 months = `adequate`; 3-9 = `sparse`; <3 = `cold_start`; lookup error = `unknown` (transparent fallback, never crashes the DPR path). Wired into the per-analysis DPR data assembler at [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) (running in Promise.all alongside counterfactualImpact + orgCalibration + dataLifecycle); rendered as a dedicated FEEDBACK ADEQUACY · {VERDICT} strip on page 1 of every DPR right below Org Calibration via [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts). Specimen DPR seeded with a sparse-verdict example at [sample-dpr.ts](src/lib/reports/sample-dpr.ts). Cold-start posture is honest: "Per Kahneman & Klein (2009), this is insufficient closed-loop feedback for intuition to be calibrated; treat experience-based claims with the same scrutiny as a cold-start audit." **Education Room flashcards** (advanced tier, kahneman_klein tag): `bias_illusion_of_validity`, `bias_prospective_hindsight`, `bias_feedback_adequacy` in the cognitive_biases deck. **Chat coaching** updated in [founder-context.ts](src/app/api/founder-hub/founder-context.ts) so the AI references all three by name when the founder asks about Kahneman & Klein, R²F operationalisation, overconfident memos, or pre-mortem coaching. **Why this matters**: R²F is the single most defensible positioning asset on the landing page; until 2026-04-30 it was claimed but only partially operationalised. The 2009 paper has at least 10 distinct findings worth implementing — these three are #5 / #3 / #6 of that ranked list (the next 7 are surfaced in the same sprint commit message for sequencing). **Forward-looking rule**: when extending R²F further, reach for the ranked remaining-7 list before adding new R²F surfaces. Adding paper-grounded detectors (vs. heuristic ones) is what makes the moat citable; every new detector should land with the academic anchor in `bias-education.ts academicReference` and an Education Room flashcard in the same commit.
- **Outcome Gate Enforcement (locked 2026-04-26 — Phase 1, the structural fix for the cathedral-of-code trap):** [src/lib/learning/outcome-gate.ts](src/lib/learning/outcome-gate.ts) `checkOutcomeGate(userId, enforce: boolean = false)` now returns `allowed: false` at HARD threshold when `enforce=true`. [src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) POST looks up `Organization.enforceOutcomeGate` for any org the user belongs to (via TeamMember); if any org has it `true`, the gate enforces. When blocked, returns HTTP 409 with `code: 'OUTCOME_GATE_BLOCKED'` + `pendingCount` + `pendingAnalysisIds` + `level: 'hard'` so the client can route the user to the outcome reporter. Org default = `false` preserves the legacy soft-nudge experience for free / individual / non-design-partner accounts. Design partners flip the flag to `true` as a contractual term of the partnership — the data flywheel becomes contractual, not aspirational. Founder School lesson `es_11` codifies the discovery-call language ("three things are non-negotiable: workflow mapping in this call, audit-before-meeting, outcome-gate enforced at platform level"). **Phase 2 (shipped 2026-04-26 — see Outcome Gate Phase 2 lock above) and Phase 3 (shipped 2026-04-27 — see Outcome Gate Phase 3 lock below)** complete the wiring: the modal now pre-fills the outcome value from auto-detected drafts and routes the submit through `PATCH /api/outcomes/draft action='confirm'` for one-click resolution, with a fallback to manual `POST /api/outcomes` when the user overrides. Migration: `prisma/migrations/20260426170000_add_org_enforce_outcome_gate/migration.sql` adds the `enforceOutcomeGate` column. **Why this matters**: NotebookLM Q6 pre-mortem (saved as note `9a249bd8` in master KB `809f5104`) identified outcome-gate avoidance as the structural failure mode that kills the first paid conversion — the platform now enforces the workflow change so the founder doesn't have to be the heavy in every conversation.

- **Outcome Gate Phase 3 · auto-draft prefill (locked 2026-04-27 — completes the flywheel-friction collapse):** [OutcomeGateModal](src/components/ui/OutcomeGate.tsx) now fetches `/api/outcomes/draft` on mount, builds a `Map<analysisId, DraftOutcome>` filtered to the gate's pending list, and pre-fills the outcome value when the user picks an analysis with a matching draft. UI changes: (a) analysis-list rows render a "Draft ready" pill with Lightbulb icon when a draft exists for that analysis (title attribute carries source + confidence); (b) when an analysis with a draft is selected, an indigo-tinted info pill appears above the outcome buttons showing source name, confidence percent, the first 90 chars of the draft's evidence quote, and "Pre-filled below — confirm to log, or change to override"; (c) the submit button label switches between "Confirm draft outcome" and "Submit & Unlock Analysis" based on whether the user kept or overrode the auto-detected outcome value. **Submission paths**: confirm-path → `PATCH /api/outcomes/draft action='confirm'` (server creates the DecisionOutcome, marks the analysis status, triggers recalibration in one transaction via `confirmDraftOutcome` in [outcome-inference.ts](src/lib/learning/outcome-inference.ts)). Override-path → `POST /api/outcomes` with the user's chosen outcome, plus a fire-and-forget `PATCH /api/outcomes/draft action='dismiss'` to clear the now-stale draft (never block the success path on draft cleanup). **Why this matters**: per CLAUDE.md Unicorn Roadmap pitfalls, Cloverpop's "manual logging adoption trap" is the canonical risk — Outcome Gate enforcement (Phase 1) only compounds the data moat if friction collapses (Phase 3). 3-click → 1-click is the highest-leverage UX move on the moat-data accumulation curve.

- **Demo → account claim flow (locked 2026-04-27 — D9 Tier 2 ship; closes the broken-funnel hole where every wow-moment audit was a dead end):** [`/api/onboarding/claim-demo-analysis`](src/app/api/onboarding/claim-demo-analysis/route.ts) accepts `{ analysisId | documentId }` and atomically transfers `Document.userId` from `DEMO_USER_ID` to the authenticated user via `updateMany` with a predicate (race-safe; two simultaneous claims can't both succeed). 24h window from `Document.uploadedAt` (matches the per-IP demo rate-limit so older audits have already aged out). MOVE semantics — the demo URL stops working post-claim, mental model stays clean. Audit log: new `CLAIM_DEMO_ANALYSIS` action. **Flow**: [/demo](src/app/demo/page.tsx)'s [PasteAuditResults](src/components/marketing/demo/PasteAuditResults.tsx) Save CTA routes to `/login?mode=signup&redirect=/onboarding/claim?demoAnalysisId={id}&demoDocumentId={id}`. [/onboarding/claim](src/app/onboarding/claim/page.tsx) is a thin client page that auth-checks (bounces to login with self as redirect), POSTs to the API, and redirects to `/documents/[id]?claimed=true`. Doc detail page reads `?claimed=true` on mount, fires a "Audit claimed from your demo run" success toast, and strips the param from the URL so a refresh doesn't re-fire. **Failure modes**: 401 (unauthed → login redirect); 404 (audit not found); 410 (window expired or already claimed); 409 (lost race); 503 (transient). Each surfaces a specific UI message + retry CTA when retryable. **Why this matters**: per CLAUDE.md the demo runs the real 12-node pipeline at ~£0.40 per audit; without the claim flow, every wow moment was orphaned and the conversion was a cold sign-up to an empty dashboard. Now the visitor lands on THEIR audit at /documents/[id], with the same DQI score and bias list visible.

- **Decision Knowledge Graph share flow (locked 2026-04-27 — A2 Tier 2 ship; sales artefact a CSO can DM):** new Prisma model [GraphShareLink](prisma/schema.prisma) with snapshot Json field — at share-time the server captures the org's current [GraphNetworkReport](src/lib/reports/graph-report.ts) and stores it as JSON. The public viewer renders THAT snapshot, not live data — protects against future audits leaking via shared URLs and lets the public route work without auth context. Public read at [GET /api/graph-share/[token]](src/app/api/graph-share/[token]/route.ts) — no auth required; password-gated shares return 401 with `requiresPassword: true` and accept the password via POST. View counter increments fire-and-forget on each successful read. **Sharer UX**: [GraphShareModal](src/components/visualizations/GraphShareModal.tsx) opens from the new "Share graph" button in the [/dashboard/decision-graph](<src/app/(platform)/dashboard/decision-graph/page.tsx>) header (next to SVG/PNG export). Submit creates the link + swaps the modal body to a copy-URL view with viewer count + revoke option (inline confirm prompt, NOT `window.confirm` — per CLAUDE.md native-dialog ban on wow-moment surfaces). **Public viewer** at [/shared/graph/[token]](src/app/shared/graph/[token]/page.tsx) — navy watermark header with sharer label + capture date + view count + expiry; redaction notice when active; 4-stat row (decisions / outcomes / bias patterns / network density); risk state with severity badge; top influential nodes; structural anti-patterns with severity color-coding; CTA footer ("Build your own Decision Knowledge Graph · Start your trial"). Empty-state for snapshots with 0 nodes. Mobile-friendly grid layout. New `GRAPH_SHARE_CREATED` + `GRAPH_SHARE_REVOKED` audit actions. **Why this matters**: per the original Tier 2 brainstorm — the compounding moat stays a marketing claim until a contributor can DEMONSTRATE it to a peer. Now a CSO can DM a `/shared/graph/[token]` URL to her CFO + open the audit committee meeting with "here's what strategy has been catching this quarter."

- **ICP / positioning constants extraction (locked 2026-04-28 — C1):** [src/lib/constants/icp.ts](src/lib/constants/icp.ts) is the single canonical source for the locked positioning vocabulary that previously lived as prose in three places (founder-context.ts MARKET STRATEGY block, the Expansion line, the FOUNDER NOTES ICP lead, and StartHereTab.tsx Current Positioning Anchor card). They are NOT dead code; do NOT delete them.** When ANY tab is added/renamed/consolidated, the cascade is now THREE routing tables in lockstep — `LEGACY_TAB_REDIRECTS` + `TAB_NAV_TARGETS` + the founder-context `[[nav]]` list — plus SEARCH_INDEX. A future audit that finds chat-nav/founder-context drift should reconcile against the `TabId` union, not propose deleting by-reference components.

- **C4 empathic-mode Discovery card — CLAIM RE-CORRECTED 2026-05-18 (the 2026-05-17 correction was ITSELF materially false — the inverse failure).** Chain of record: (a) the 2026-04-28 lock claimed /dashboard renders [DiscoveryGradeImpactCard](src/components/discovery/DiscoveryGradeImpactCard.tsx) `variant="post-upload"`; (b) the 2026-05-17 friction audit then asserted via `rg` that the component has "ZERO mount sites anywhere — not /dashboard, not /demo… it is dead code… re-mounting on /demo NOT done here"; (c) **the 2026-05-18 grep proves it is LIVE-mounted on BOTH surfaces right now** — [src/app/demo/page.tsx:573](src/app/demo/page.tsx) (`variant="static"` + `STATIC_DEMO_ANCHOR`, inside the `idleState` cold-landing block — it is the FIRST thing every wedge DM prospect sees on /demo) AND [src/app/(platform)/dashboard/page.tsx:1616](<src/app/(platform)/dashboard/page.tsx>). The `git log -S` pickaxe shows NO post-2026-05-17 re-mount commit (only the original add `21c23a45` + a refine `f5b780b3`), so the 2026-05-17 "ZERO mounts" `rg` was a **false negative** — the multi-line import form (`DiscoveryGradeImpactCard,\n  …\n} from '@/components/discovery/…'`) + the JSX usage evaded its single-line pattern. The component was NOT dead; the cold empathic surface has been live on /demo the whole time. **The decision-roi.ts:8 comment ("was dead code") is stale by the same chain — back-fill on next touch of that file.** Forward rule (sharpened): a mount claim — in EITHER direction ("is rendered on X" OR "is dead / ZERO mounts") — requires a grep that proves it, and the grep MUST be resilient to multi-line imports (match the JSX usage `<ComponentName` AND the `from '…/ComponentName'` import path, never a single-line `import { … ComponentName … }` pattern). A false "it's dead" is the same M-1 failure class as a false "it's mounted", and it is worse when the lock then instructs future sessions "do not re-flag" — that buries a live, load-bearing surface.

- **Friction audit #2 + #3 — persistent per-org ROI surface + hot-path loop-close (locked 2026-05-17).** The core-flow friction audit found (a) the retention/moat thesis ("embeddedness with MEASURABLE ROI", which the Phase-1 graduation gate is scored on) had no live product surface, and (b) the only post-analysis loop-close prompt was a 30-day-aged sticky pill — nothing asked at the wow moment.
