### Visualization Components (light-theme audit rule)

- Visualization cards (`ToxicCombinationCard`, `RiskHeatMap`, `GraphDetailPanel`, `DecisionTimeline`, `StakeholderMap`) keep dark-theme Tailwind classes **inside** their colored severity wrappers (`bg-red-950/40`, `bg-amber-950/20`) — that is correct, the interior is dark.
- The audit rule: check only the **outermost** heading and elements that sit directly on the page surface. Any `text-white` on a standalone heading outside a dark wrapper is a bug. Interiors on red/amber/yellow severity cards can stay dark.
- Same rule for `ActivityFeed` — rendered inside a platform `.card` (light), so its row content uses `var(--text-primary/secondary/muted)`, not `text-white` or `text-gray-400`.

### DQI Grade Boundaries (locked)

- Canonical grade scale: A 85+, B 70+, C 55+, D 40+, F 0+ — matches `src/lib/scoring/dqi.ts` → `GRADE_THRESHOLDS`.
- The JSDoc at the top of `dqi.ts` is the external reference. **Update both** the comment AND `GRADE_THRESHOLDS` when changing boundaries, or the published contract drifts from runtime.

### Sparkles Icon Discipline (locked 2026-04-26)

`Sparkles` from `lucide-react` is the universal "built with AI" tell — banned on every category pill, badge, and eyebrow chip on every marketing surface and on every public share view. Audit this rule whenever adding a new badge or pill on `(marketing)/**` or `src/app/shared/**`. The 2026-04-26 sweep stripped Sparkles from `FeaturedDeepCases.tsx`, `CaseStudyGrid.tsx`, `case-studies/sample/[slug]/page.tsx`, and two sites in `shared/[token]/page.tsx`. Two exceptions stay legal: (1) the AI Copilot surface chrome at `/dashboard/ask` (Sparkles next to the chat composer reads as "this is an AI surface" and is on-brand for the assistant pattern), (2) the Free-tier "N free this month" reassurance chip on `/dashboard` (platform chrome, not marketing). Every other Sparkles needs a justification or it gets cut.

### Sitemap SSOT Discipline (locked 2026-05-18 — Google Search Console indexing fix)

[src/app/sitemap.ts](src/app/sitemap.ts) `STATIC_ROUTES` is the single source of truth for the XML sitemap. **Inclusion rule:** a marketing route belongs in `STATIC_ROUTES` iff it (a) returns 200 (never a redirect), (b) is NOT `robots: { index: false }`, and (c) is a real content surface a search visitor should land on. **When you add a new public marketing page, add it to `STATIC_ROUTES` in the SAME commit** — an indexable page absent from the sitemap is organic-discovery suppression, which for a customer-acquisition-priority company is a load-bearing bug, not a nicety. The 2026-05-18 Google Search Console audit caught the prior flat sitemap omitting **14** high-value indexable pages (pricing / security / how-it-works / proof / bias-genome / r2f-standard / trust / taxonomy / onepager / decision-provenance / regulatory-ai-verify / simulate-ceo) while wrongly including `/login` (utility, zero indexable content → manufactures the "Crawled - currently not indexed" GSC signal).

**Deliberately excluded — do NOT "fix" by adding (each is correct):** `/login` (utility); `/calibration` (in-component `redirect()` → `/r2f-standard#calibration`); `/decision-alpha` (308 → `/proof`); the 3 deliberate `robots:{index:false}` pages — `/decision-intel-for-boards`, `/design-partner` (unlisted 5-seat program), `/pricing/quote` (public quote builder). Sitemapping a noindex page is a conflicting-signal SEO anti-pattern; sitemapping a redirect manufactures the "Page with redirect" GSC signal. The inline header in `sitemap.ts` names every exclusion + why — read it before adding/removing.

**robots.ts is correct as-is — do NOT touch it.** It blocks `/api/ /dashboard/ /shared/` (right tool for app/api/share-links; the "Blocked by robots.txt" GSC count is those URLs and is working-as-intended, NOT a bug). The 3 noindex marketing pages correctly use the `noindex` **meta tag**, never robots-disallow — robots-disallowing them would prevent Google from _seeing_ the noindex tag (a known anti-pattern that leaves URL-only entries in results). Never add a marketing path to the robots `disallow` list to "hide" it; use page-level `robots:{index:false}` metadata.

**Founder-verify items (NOT code-fixable from the repo — surfaced 2026-05-18, do not auto-change):** (1) `sitemap.ts` + `robots.ts` + `layout.tsx` all default `siteUrl` to `https://www.decision-intel.com` (www) via `NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL || <www fallback>`. The GSC property is the `sc-domain:decision-intel.com` domain property. Confirm prod `NEXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL` is set to the **actual canonical domain** (apex vs www must match DNS + the canonical `<link>`), or a www↔apex redirect inflates "Page with redirect". Changing the fallback is prod-env-dependent + unverifiable from the repo — a founder DNS/Vercel-env check, never a blind code edit. (2) "Not found (404) · 3" + "Page with redirect · 3" are URL-level — open the GSC row to see the exact URLs; the only in-code lever (sitemap purity = never emit a 404/redirect URL) is now shipped, so any residual is old external links hitting the intentional 308s (`/decision-alpha`, `/calibration`, retired `/dashboard/*`), which is exactly what those 308s are FOR (Google dropping them is the goal — not a bug to chase).

### NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS Discipline (locked 2026-04-26, hardened 2026-04-27)

Every new `Nudge.nudgeType` enum value MUST land with a label in [src/lib/constants/human-audit.ts](src/lib/constants/human-audit.ts) `NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS` IN THE SAME COMMIT. The 2026-04-26 audit caught `bias_comment_mention` (shipped commit bf6b038, ~Apr 22) had no label entry — every @mention nudge in the dashboard `NudgeWidget` and `NudgesPageContent` rendered the raw enum string instead of "Comment Mention" for ~4 days. The render fallback (`|| nudge.nudgeType`) hides this from compile-time checks; the test you want is "manually create a Nudge with the new type and verify the label renders." Before adding a new nudgeType: search `NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS` and add the label. The 2026-04-27 audit caught FIVE more missing entries: `toxic_combination`, `pre_decision_coaching`, `document_access_granted`, `bias_task_assigned`, `playbook_followup`. These had been shipping silently for weeks across 7+ creator sites. All five added in the same sweep; a comment block above the labels map now records the discipline so future sessions search `nudgeType:` first. **Defensive move**: when adding a NEW nudge creation site, run `rg -nP "nudgeType:\s*['\"][a-z_]+['\"]" src/ --type=ts | rg -v "test\.ts"` and verify every distinct value appears in `NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS`. If you find a new value that's used in two places but missing from labels, that's a bug — not a feature request.

### Onborda Tour Registration Discipline (locked 2026-04-26)

Every role added to `Role = 'cso' | 'ma' | 'bizops' | 'pe_vc' | 'other'` MUST also be registered in the Onborda steps array at [OnboardingTour.tsx](src/components/onboarding/OnboardingTour.tsx) `OnboardingTourProvider`. Defining `TOUR_STEPS_BY_ROLE.<role>` and `TOUR_NAME_BY_ROLE.<role>` is NOT enough — Onborda needs the explicit `{ tour: 'dashboard-tour-<role>', steps: TOUR_STEPS_BY_ROLE.<role> }` entry or the tour silently never fires (users fall through to the default 'dashboard-tour'). The 2026-04-26 audit caught pe_vc was missing the registration even though everything else cascaded correctly — runtime bug, no compile error.

### WelcomeModal v3.5 HXC-first merge (locked 2026-05-11)

The first-login gate is now a single merged modal (no more two-step WelcomeModal → Phase1PersonaModal back-to-back). [WelcomeModal](src/components/ui/WelcomeModal.tsx) asks the v3.5 HXC question directly using `PHASE_1_PERSONAS` as the canonical taxonomy (Fractional CSO / Mid-market Corp Dev / Smaller-fund GP / PE-backed Founder / Other → **full platform access + generic overview, NOT waitlisted** — see the 2026-05-19 amendment below). The legacy `onboardingRole` enum (cso / ma / bizops / pe_vc / other) is auto-derived server-side from `phase1Persona` via the new helper `phase1PersonaToOnboardingRole` in [icp.ts](src/lib/constants/icp.ts) — so the entire downstream cascade (OnboardingTour, sample bundles, role-empty-states, FirstRunInlineWalkthrough, useOnboardingRole, RoleSamplePicker) keeps reading `onboardingRole` unchanged. Mapping: fractional_cso → cso · midmarket_corp_dev → ma · pe_backed_founder → ma (acquisition + IC memo workflow overlay) · smaller_fund_gp → pe_vc · other → other.

[Phase1PersonaModal](src/components/onboarding/Phase1PersonaModal.tsx) stays mounted on `(platform)/layout.tsx` as a **legacy backfill component** — its early returns (`!data.onboardingCompleted` || `data.phase1Persona`) make it a no-op for new users (who complete the merged WelcomeModal with both fields set atomically). It only fires for users who completed the pre-2026-05-11 broad-role flow and still have `phase1Persona = null`. SAFE TO DELETE once `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM "UserSettings" WHERE onboardingCompleted = true AND phase1Persona IS NULL` returns 0.

**Why the merge happened:** the prior two-modal flow asked variations of the same question back-to-back. Founder caught it in screenshot 2026-05-11. Per CLAUDE.md positioning, persona signal is captured ONCE at sign-up; the v3.5 HXC narrowing is the right level of granularity for both the Vohra HXC PMF cohort filter AND the downstream personalization (Tour / sample bundles / empty states / first-run walkthrough). The merged flow drops the two-step friction without losing either signal.

**Forward-looking rule:** when `PHASE_1_PERSONAS` changes (new persona, label tweak, hxcEligible flip), edit `PHASE_1_PERSONAS` in `icp.ts` first, then `VALUE_PROPS_BY_PERSONA` + `PERSONA_ICON` in `WelcomeModal.tsx` in the same commit. The TypeScript `Record<Phase1PersonaId, ...>` shapes enforce this at compile time. When a new sign-up GATE file ships (e.g., a dedicated `/signup` form route), add its path to `ONBOARDING_GATE_FILES` in [scripts/audit-platform.mjs](scripts/audit-platform.mjs) so the `onboarding-persona-drift` check verifies the new gate references HXC personas.

**AMENDMENT 2026-05-19 — access ≠ cohort: "Other"/non-wedge is NO LONGER waitlisted; it gets FULL platform access with the generic overview.** Founder-directed. The strategy is UNCHANGED: the 4-persona wedge, the Vohra ≥40% HXC graduation gate, and the cold-context marketing narrowing all stand verbatim. What changed: the `Other` selection (and any non-wedge persona) used to hit a discouraging waitlist-framed interstitial ("we'll keep you posted… may not be tuned for your use case… we'll reach out when the platform extends") with an empty value-prop. That is removed. `Other` now renders the SAME standard value-prop card + the SAME completion CTAs (tour / upload / sample, all → `completeOnboarding`) as the HXC personas, just with a **generic-overview** `VALUE_PROPS_BY_PERSONA.other` (real bullets: 22-bias R²F on any memo / DPR on every audit / Decision Knowledge Graph compounds) + an optional non-waitlist role free-text. **The `hxcEligible:false` tag on the `other` persona in `icp.ts` is LOAD-BEARING and intentionally UNCHANGED** — it is a _cohort discriminator_, not an access gate: `/api/onboarding` still derives `phase1HxcEligible=false` for `other` server-side, so they stay EXCLUDED from the Vohra ≥40%-HXC graduation-gate measurement (signal integrity) and are NOT Outcome-Gate-enforced (`/api/analyze/stream` keys enforcement on `phase1HxcEligible=true`). **Rationale:** the v3.5 narrowing's own text says it is the "ENFORCED narrowing on **cold-context**"; a founder you are personally talking to who wants to try it + refer it is _warm_ traffic — walling them off severs a referral edge for zero strategic gain while still polluting nothing (the cohort tag protects the metric). Code: `handleOtherSubmit` / the `other_thanks` step / the `step` state machine were deleted from both [WelcomeModal](src/components/ui/WelcomeModal.tsx) AND the legacy [Phase1PersonaModal](src/components/onboarding/Phase1PersonaModal.tsx) (parallel-fixed for consistency); `icp.ts` `other` description + `/api/onboarding` comment updated; the route LOGIC was already correct (no migration). **Forward-looking rule: NEVER flip `hxcEligible:true` on `other` to "let them in" — they are already fully in; flipping it pollutes the Vohra graduation metric. Access is a UI/flow concern; cohort is the `hxcEligible` flag. Keep them separate.**

### audit-platform.mjs SEMANTIC drift category (added 2026-05-11)

The platform audit script gained a 5th check category: SEMANTIC drift. Added `checkOnboardingPersonaCoherence` after the WelcomeModal v3.5-drift miss — the structural checks (modal-shape / native-dialog / dark-tokens / hex / H1) all passed clean on a welcome modal that was technically valid but semantically out-of-date against CLAUDE.md GTM locks. The new check fires `onboarding-persona-drift` (severity high, category stale) when a sign-up GATE file (explicit allowlist at `ONBOARDING_GATE_FILES` in the script) defines a role taxonomy without referencing v3.5 HXC personas (`fractional_cso` / `midmarket_corp_dev` / `smaller_fund_gp` / `pe_backed_founder`) or the canonical `PHASE_1_PERSONAS` export or the bridge helper `phase1PersonaToOnboardingRole`. Downstream consumer files (OnboardingTour / sample-bundles / role-empty-states / FirstRunInlineWalkthrough) are NOT in the allowlist and are correctly skipped — the legacy 5-role enum is legitimate there via the bridge.

**When to extend with new SEMANTIC checks:** every time a future audit catches drift between code and a CLAUDE.md lock that the structural checks missed, add a new `check<Name>` function to the SEMANTIC category. Examples queued: `checkLockedVocabularyDrift` (deprecated phrases like "protect outcomes" / "decision hygiene" still appearing in copy beyond what `lint-positioning.mjs` already covers), `checkPricingTierDrift` (stale tier labels / prices on consumer-facing surfaces vs canonical `PLANS` in `stripe.ts`).

### Stripe / Commerce Dedup Discipline (locked 2026-04-26, extended 2026-04-27)

Any `findFirst` query that gates a Stripe checkout (active-purchase dedup, subscription state, idempotency check) MUST fail-closed on query failure, not silently fall through to a "looks like nothing exists" branch. The 2026-04-26 audit caught `src/app/api/stripe/deal-audit/route.ts:61` was wrapped in `.catch(() => null)`, which would have let the route create a NEW Stripe checkout session for an already-purchased deal on a transient DB error → double-charge the customer. The fix pattern: explicit `try/catch` around the dedup, log the error, return a 503 "Could not verify purchase state. Please retry." Cron-side dedups (e.g. `usage-nudges/route.ts` NotificationLog idempotency check) follow the same rule for the same reason — silent fallthrough → duplicate-send. The fail-closed rule applies wherever the next action is irreversible (charge, send email, post Slack, write blockchain). For pure UI fetches the silent-warn pattern is still acceptable. The 2026-04-27 audit applied the same rule to `src/app/api/stripe/checkout/route.ts:42` — subscription lookup before customer-reuse was `.catch(() => null)`, which on a transient DB failure would silently skip the customer-reuse path and create a duplicate Stripe customer record. Different consequence than deal-audit (duplicate customer, not double-charge) but same fail-open class. Hardened to fail-closed with 503 retry-please. **Forward-looking rule**: every NEW route that contains a Stripe `checkout.sessions.create` call must have its preceding lookup queries fail-closed in the same commit. No silent catches between auth and Stripe.

### Count-then-create race discipline + analysis-quota reservation (locked 2026-06-06)

**Why this lock exists.** A 2026-06-06 enforcement-gate audit (3 parallel bidirectional grep-before-assert sweeps; authz inner-gates + fail-open commerce + tenant isolation all came back CLEAN) confirmed the codebase's authorization discipline, but found **count-then-create concurrency races** on every enforced limit that wasn't already locked. Under Postgres READ COMMITTED a bare `count()`-then-`create()` is NOT atomic: two concurrent requests both read `used = limit-1`, both pass, both insert. **The canonical fix is an interactive `$transaction` that takes a lock BEFORE the count** — either `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` on the owning row (seat caps, keyed on the Organization row) or `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('<domain>'), hashtext(<userId>))` (per-user caps). Routes hardened this session: `team/invite/accept` (FOR UPDATE), `webhooks` (advisory, MAX_WEBHOOKS_PER_USER), `team/invite` + `team/invite/bulk` (FOR UPDATE — seat cap now atomic at the invite layer too, not just accept).

**The analysis-quota cost race — reservation pattern.** `/api/analyze/stream` (line ~123) and the shared `analyzeDocument` (`src/lib/analysis/analyzer.ts`, behind 7 entry points) ran `checkAnalysisLimit` BEFORE the ~£0.40 / ~17-LLM-call pipeline, but the `Analysis` row is only created AFTER it — so a lock around the insert can't un-spend the money. The fix RESERVES the slot before the work: **`reserveAnalysisSlot(userId, containerId?)` / `releaseAnalysisSlot(reservationId)` in [plan-limits.ts](src/lib/utils/plan-limits.ts)**, backed by the additive `AnalysisReservation` table (migration `20260606120000_analysis_quota_reservation` — **FOUNDER must `npx prisma migrate deploy` lock-step with deploy**; same additive-zero-risk pattern as every FounderOs\* table). Under a per-user advisory lock it sweeps stale reservations (TTL `ANALYSIS_RESERVATION_TTL_MS = 15min`, crash safety), counts this-month analyses PLUS live reservations, then inserts a reservation or denies. The caller MUST `releaseAnalysisSlot` on EVERY exit path (the stream route releases on doc-lock-409 + outer setup-catch + stream success/error/cancel; `analyzeDocument` releases in a `finally`); a crash is swept by TTL. **Unlimited plans (Team/Enterprise/admin/container-purchase) → `reservationId: null`, no row.** **Schema drift (table not migrated) → fails OPEN to the legacy non-atomic check** (worst case is the pre-existing race, never a blocked audit). **Score-neutral by construction** — zero changes to `src/lib/agents/` / scoring / DQI / persistence; the held-out `dqi-distribution-check` is byte-identical (hashes unchanged), so NO methodology bump. Tests: `plan-limits.test.ts` (8 new reservation/release cases incl. the cost-race + fail-open-on-drift + idempotent-release invariants); stream + benchmark mocks gained `reserveAnalysisSlot`/`releaseAnalysisSlot`.

**Sibling race classes hardened (2026-06-06, second sweep).** Two more agent-found concurrency classes, verified bidirectional + fixed (ripple-alerts "over-fetch" was a FALSE POSITIVE — the detector uses both `decisionFrame` + `outcome.summary`; bias-comments fire-and-forget is documented-intentional; both correctly dropped). (a) **JSON read-modify-write on a column** — `decisions/[id]/priors` (microPredictions append), `decisions/[id]/pmi-signals` POST+PATCH (signals append/observe), `containers/[id]/proxy-resolution` (proxy resolve) all read a JSON array, mutated it in JS, and wrote it back — two concurrent writes lose one. Each now locks the parent `DecisionContainer` row (`SELECT id … FOR UPDATE`) and RE-READS the JSON inside the transaction before re-applying the existing pure helper. (b) **Check-then-act on room status** — `decision-rooms/[id]/blind-priors/{reveal,distribute}` read `blindPriorRevealedAt`/`status` then acted; reveal could double-send emails + double-audit. Both now use an atomic guarded `updateMany({ where: { id, <precondition> }, data })` + `count===0 → 409`, with the read-check kept as a fast pre-check. (c) **UTC quota boundary** — `plan-limits.ts` `startOfCurrentMonthUtc()` replaces a local-time `new Date()+setDate(1)+setHours(0)` that drifts the monthly window on a non-UTC host (prod is UTC, so score/quota-neutral today; correctness hardening).

**Forward-looking rules.** (1) **Every NEW plan-limited create path that runs an expensive/irreversible op gates with `reserveAnalysisSlot` + a `finally` release, never a bare `checkAnalysisLimit`-then-create** (`checkAnalysisLimit` stays the read-only display/early-reject helper). (2) Every NEW per-org/per-user COUNT cap (seats, webhooks, future quotas) does the count+insert inside one interactive `$transaction` with `FOR UPDATE`/advisory lock — never two separate statements. The SSOT for the reservation shape is `reserveAnalysisSlot`; never inline a parallel reservation. (3) When the reservation table or TTL changes, edit `plan-limits.ts` + the test invariants in lockstep. (4) The fail-open-on-schema-drift posture is deliberate (additive table) — never "harden" it to fail-closed; that would block legitimate audits on pre-migration deployments. (5) **Any read-modify-write on a JSON column (append/merge to a stored array/map) must lock the owning row + re-read inside a `$transaction`** — a bare read-then-write loses concurrent updates; (6) **any check-then-act on a row's status must use an atomic guarded `updateMany`** (precondition in the WHERE, `count===0` ⇒ 409) before firing side-effects (emails/audit) — never trust a prior read.

### Cron Observability Discipline (locked 2026-05-25, maintenance audit)

The cron dispatcher at [/api/cron/dispatch](src/app/api/cron/dispatch/route.ts) is a single Vercel cron entry that fans out to ~19 sub-routes daily (sync-intelligence, outreach-intel, detect-outcomes, proxy-resolution, infer-graph-edges, retry-nudges, google-drive-sync, daily-linkedin, enforce-retention, vohra-pmf-trigger, cache/cleanup + Sunday: learn-toxic-patterns, recalibrate + Monday: outcome-reminders, team-profiles, weekly-digest). Until 2026-05-25, per-job success/failure was visible ONLY in Vercel stdout logs (`vercel logs --follow`) and the dispatcher's HTTP response. A dispatcher timeout or silent failure meant a week of dark crons with no historical signal — the Vohra HXC PMF gate, outcome-recalibration moat, and learn-toxic-patterns sharpening all depend on these crons, and a multi-day outage was structurally invisible.

**What shipped**: [CronRun](prisma/schema.prisma) Prisma model (one row per cron-route × dispatch-invocation; migration `20260525120100_cron_run_observability`). [instrumentCronJob](src/lib/utils/cron-instrumentation.ts) wrapper that opens a `running` row at start, closes with status / durationMs / error / httpStatus at end. Writes are FAIL-SOFT — a CronRun persistence error NEVER breaks the cron itself (observability degradation is preferable to cron breakage). [12-test vitest suite](src/lib/utils/cron-instrumentation.test.ts) locks the contract: returns runJob's result unchanged on success + error; opens row at start with status='running'; closes row with terminal status; truncates long error messages to 500 chars; catches thrown errors and records them; proceeds without persistence when both create AND update fail. Dispatch route wraps each sub-route call (including its retry pair) in `instrumentCronJob`. New admin surface at [/api/admin/cron-health](src/app/api/admin/cron-health/route.ts) returns per-route `lastRunAt` / `lastSuccessAt` / `lastFailureAt` + `lastError` + `consecutiveFailures` + `averageDurationMs` + last 30 runs, plus a procurement-grade summary block (`routesWithCriticalFailures` = consecutive ≥3, `routesStaleOver48h`). Admin-gated via `isAdminUserId(user.id)`.

**Forward-looking rule**: any new cron route added to the dispatcher's `dailyJobs` / `sundayJobs` / `mondayJobs` arrays inherits CronRun persistence automatically — no extra wiring needed; the wrapper sits at the dispatch-loop level. When adding cron-like background work OUTSIDE the dispatcher (e.g. a direct Vercel cron entry, a webhook-triggered async job), wrap the work in `instrumentCronJob(route, fn)` so it shares the same observability surface. Never re-implement the persistence shape — the SSOT is `cron-instrumentation.ts`, same drift-class discipline as the canonical-imports lock. CronRun retention is governed by the existing `/api/cron/enforce-retention` cadence; if a different retention floor is ever needed for cron observability specifically, add it there, not in the wrapper.

### Bias Taxonomy

- **22 biases with stable taxonomy IDs: DI-B-001 through DI-B-022** (defined in `src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts`). **DI-B-021 (illusion_of_validity)** and **DI-B-022 (inside_view_dominance)** were added 2026-04-30 as part of the Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint (anchored on the 2009 paper for DI-B-021 and Kahneman & Lovallo 2003 "Delusions of Success" HBR for DI-B-022).
- These IDs are permanent and published at `/taxonomy`. Never renumber or reassign them.
- Biases are referenced by snake_case string keys (e.g., `confirmation_bias`, `anchoring_bias`, `illusion_of_validity`, `inside_view_dominance`).
- **Adding a new bias is a load-bearing cascade.** When DI-B-023 lands, every one of these surfaces must update in the same commit: (1) `BiasCategory` union in `src/types/index.ts`, (2) `BIAS_CATEGORIES` map in the same file, (3) `BIAS_EDUCATION` entry in `src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts`, (4) `ALIASES` map in `src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts` so LLM display-name output normalizes back, (5) `BIAS_DETECTIVE_PROMPT` taxonomy enumeration + (6) any compound interactions + (7) any toxic combinations in `src/lib/agents/prompts.ts`, (8) the `forgottenQuestions` taxonomy enum count in the same file (currently "33-bias taxonomy"), (9) Education Room flashcard in `src/components/founder-hub/education/education-room-data.ts` cognitive_biases deck, (10) this CLAUDE.md count + ID range, (11) `INTERACTION_MATRIX` extension in `src/lib/ontology/interaction-matrix.ts` — add the new bias as both a row AND a column on every existing row + add a row for its self-axis (every entry must be present, no implicit defaults). The matrix-extension test at `src/lib/ontology/interaction-matrix.test.ts` asserts `MATRIX_BIAS_KEYS` is a superset of `BIAS_EDUCATION` keys; CI fails loudly if the taxonomy grows without the matrix extending. The discriminated-union BiasCategory will fail compilation loudly if any consumer is missed — trust the type system but do the cascade in one PR.

### JURISDICTION_REGISTRY refactor (locked 2026-05-13 — F-3 ship)

- **Closes the audit's F-3 brainstorm** that's been carried since the 2026-05-01 deep refinement audit: "buildSovereignContextBlock in agents/prompts.ts hand-codes each EM jurisdiction (refactor to JURISDICTION_REGISTRY would unlock fast moat scaling for Rwanda / Ghana / Egypt / new African jurisdictions)". The prior implementation was ~80 lines of inline per-country `if (lc.includes(...))` branches in `prompts.ts`; adding a new jurisdiction meant editing a giant agent-pipeline file (high blast radius, no test coverage).
- **New typed SSOT** at [src/lib/data/jurisdiction-registry.ts](src/lib/data/jurisdiction-registry.ts) — 10 canonical entries (Nigeria / Kenya / Ghana / WAEMU / South Africa / Egypt / Tanzania / East-Africa peers / Argentina / Turkey). Each entry carries `id` + `label` + `triggers` (case-insensitive country aliases; WAEMU triggers on all 9 member countries individually) + `narrative` (the exact prompt-injection bullet) + `currency` + `monetaryAuthority` + `fxRegime` discriminator + optional `relatedFrameworks` list.
- **Pure-function matcher** `matchJurisdictions(countries) → JurisdictionEntry[]` returns entries in canonical registry order regardless of input order (deterministic prompt output). Multi-WAEMU-country inputs collapse to ONE bullet (e.g., a Senegal + Mali + Côte d'Ivoire memo yields one WAEMU bullet, not three). `matchJurisdictionNarratives(countries) → string[]` is the convenience wrapper the prompt consumer uses.
- **`buildSovereignContextBlock` in [agents/prompts.ts](src/lib/agents/prompts.ts)** now reads from the registry — the function body collapsed from ~80 lines of inline branches to a single `matchJurisdictionNarratives()` call. The empty-cohort + non-canonical-jurisdiction fallback messages stay in `prompts.ts` because they're the prompt-shape concern, not the per-jurisdiction concern.
- **20-test vitest suite** at [jurisdiction-registry.test.ts](src/lib/data/jurisdiction-registry.test.ts) — locks the canonical 10-entry baseline, case-insensitive matching, WAEMU multi-country collapse, registry-order output regardless of input order, defensive empty / unknown-country handling, narrative shape (must start with "• " and end with "."), trigger lowercase invariant.
- **Pipeline impact**: zero score change. The `buildSovereignContextBlock` output for any given country set is byte-identical to the pre-refactor branches — only the SOURCE of the narrative strings moved.
- **Forward-looking rule**: when adding a new jurisdiction (Rwanda-specific deeper coverage, Ghana 2025 IMF-cycle update, new African / EM regime), append to `JURISDICTION_REGISTRY` in lockstep with a regression test entry. NEVER add per-country branches to `prompts.ts` directly — the matcher + the empty-fallback path are the only allowed prompt-shape concerns. Pan-African moat scales cleanly when this rule holds.

### /r2f-standard#calibration sharpening (locked 2026-05-13 — M-4 ship)

- **Closes the audit's M-4 brainstorm** by sharpening the merged calibration section (NOT creating a new /calibration page; the route stays as a 308 redirect to `/r2f-standard#calibration` per the 2026-05-07 wedge-quad Item 2 lock).
- **Methodology version progression cards expanded** from 4 → 7 versions: adds 2.2.0 (compound risk · superseded), 2.3.0 (user-adjustable weights · live on the user-tune path · Dietvorst 2016 fix), 2.4.0 (22×22 interaction matrix · CURRENT LIVE stamp · M-1 ship 2026-05-13 covering DI-B-021 + DI-B-022). Previously the section showed only through 2.1.0 — a procurement reader asking "which methodology version produced this DPR?" got a stale answer mismatched against the actual engine stamp.
- **Tone discriminator extended** with new `current-live` (green LIVE for 2.4.0) + `superseded` (slate SUPERSEDED for 2.1.0 + 2.2.0) states. The prior `live` state is preserved for 2.3.0 (user-tune path label "LIVE (USER-TUNE PATH)") to honour that user-adjustable audits stamp 2.3.0 not 2.4.0 (the resolution chain in `computeDQI` gates user-adjustable highest precedence).
- **"Per-org Brier supersedes" honesty card sharpened** to name the Vohra HXC PMF cohort ≥5 sample-size floor (locked v3.5 graduation gate) as the COUPLED condition alongside Outcome Gate enforcement. Two gates must both fire before per-org Brier replaces the seed; the section now says so directly. Closes the procurement-question "how do you know when to switch?" without a vague hand-wave.
- **Forward-looking rule**: when METHODOLOGY_VERSION advances (e.g., M-1's 2.4.0 epoch), update the version progression cards in `R2FStandardClient.tsx` + the methodology-version-chain JSDoc in `dqi.ts` + the audit-trail prose in the M-1 (or equivalent) CLAUDE.md lock — three surfaces, one cascade. The version progression IS the procurement-grade audit trail for "which engine produced this score"; staleness on this surface defeats the purpose.

### Algorithm Aversion / Dietvorst 2016 — procurement-grade marketing beat (locked 2026-05-13 — M-5 ship)

- **Closes the audit's M-5 partial-false-negative**: the Education Room flashcards for Algorithm Aversion (`bias_algorithm_aversion`, Dietvorst, Simmons & Massey 2015 / doi:10.1037/xge0000033) AND Calibrated Rejection (`bias_calibrated_rejection`, Kahneman & Klein 2009) were ALREADY SHIPPED on the cognitive_biases deck (procurement-grade canonicalAnswers + applicationContext). The legitimate gap was buyer-facing surface coverage: zero pricing FAQ entry + zero Sparring Room rehearsal scenarios for the false-precision objection.
- **Two new buyer-facing surfaces** added 2026-05-13:
  - [Pricing FAQ entry](<src/app/(marketing)/pricing/PricingPageClient.tsx>) — _"How do I know your scoring is reliable? My team will say 'the model can't replace a CSO's judgment.'"_ The procurement-grade answer cites Dietvorst 2015 + the 2016 follow-up fix (user-adjustable weights) + the algorithm-aversion detector itself as one of the 10 R²F detectors. Lands directly on the pricing page where the buyer is doing the cost-justify reasoning that triggers algorithm aversion.
  - **Two new Sparring Room objection scenarios** at [sparring-room-data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/sparring/sparring-room-data.ts) — (a) F500 CSO (Margaret-class) raising the textbook algorithm-aversion frame ("AI questioning their judgment"); (b) Mid-market corp dev head (Damien-class, Phase 1 HXC) raising the false-precision frame ("22-bias matrix is reductive — strategic memos aren't a quant problem"). Each scenario teaches a 3-beat counter (name the pattern → reframe the artefact → close with the 2016 fix) anchored on the underlying paper (Dietvorst 2015 for CSO, Dawes 1979 + Meehl 1954 for corp dev). The founder rehearses the verbatim 30-second response under pressure.
- **Forward-looking rule**: any future R²F detector landing on the user-facing pricing surface MUST have a paired Sparring scenario for the most likely objection. The Education Room teaches the founder the literature; the Sparring Room turns the literature into a 30-second sales rehearsal; the pricing FAQ converts the rehearsed answer into a leave-behind. Three surfaces, one cascade — when adding a new detector that buyers will push back on, ship all three together.

### Vohra HXC PMF math hardening (locked 2026-05-13 — M-2 follow-through)

- **Closes the audit's M-2 false-negative** (the audit's grep for `vohra|veryDisappointed|pmf_survey` missed the existing `vohraPMFResponse` casing). Vohra infrastructure shipped 2026-05-04 — Prisma model + cron trigger + survey modal + Founder Hub tile + metrics endpoint. The legitimate gap was test coverage on `computeHxcCohortMetrics`, the load-bearing math that drives the GTM v3.5 graduation decision.
- **Two changes** in [src/lib/learning/vohra-pmf.ts](src/lib/learning/vohra-pmf.ts):
  - Extracted pure-function `aggregateHxcCohortMetrics(responses, windowStart, windowEnd)` so the math is unit-testable without a Prisma fixture. `computeHxcCohortMetrics` becomes a thin DB → pure-function wrapper.
  - **Math fix**: `graduationGatePassed` now requires BOTH N ≥ `VOHRA_PMF_KILL_MIN_N` (5) AND % ≥ 40%. Previously, the graduation gate could fire on a single "very disappointed" response (100% of 1) and declare PMF prematurely. The kill-threshold was already N-gated; this brings the graduation gate into symmetry with it. The UI tile (`VohraHxcPmfTile`) already double-gated on `sampleSize < 5 → too_early`, so this is now engine + UI in lockstep instead of UI compensating for an engine gap.
- **17-test vitest suite** at [vohra-pmf.test.ts](src/lib/learning/vohra-pmf.test.ts) — covers empty cohorts / boundary conditions / graduation gate at exactly 40% / kill threshold at exactly 30% / N-floor enforcement / per-persona breakdown / null pending responses / rounding / disjoint-gate invariant (gate + kill never fire simultaneously).
- **No Prisma migration** — the change is engine-side only.
- **Survey-window reminder (added 2026-05-15, audit §5.4 / Tip 2):** [VohraHxcPmfTile](src/components/founder-hub/start-here/VohraHxcPmfTile.tsx) now carries a "Survey window" reminder banner that fires ONLY when the gate is N-blocked (`sampleSize < killMinN`) — when the gate is live the existing status pill carries graduation/kill, so no reminder noise. The reminder is event-anchored: it reads the same `event-prep.ts` SSOT the BaftaPrepCallout uses (`getHighestPriorityUpcomingEvent` + `daysUntil`) and, when a highest-priority event is ≤45d out, frames the nudge as "send the survey before {event} — investors there will ask whether you have PMF signal" (accent reddens ≤14d). Pure date-math overlay; no new model/API. **The N-floor (`VOHRA_PMF_KILL_MIN_N`) is surfaced through the `/api/founder-hub/metrics` `pmf.killMinN` field** (server-side import) so the client tile never hardcodes the floor — same canonical-derivation discipline as `graduationThreshold`/`killThreshold` which already flow that way. `nowMs` captured via `useState(() => Date.now())` per the react-hooks/purity rule.
- **Forward-looking rule**: any new threshold gate added to the aggregator MUST be tested against the N-floor invariant in `vohra-pmf.test.ts` ("cannot fire and pass simultaneously"). The gates must remain disjoint — if a future "Phase 1.5 indicator" gate is added, it has its own N-floor + a regression test that proves it doesn't overlap with the existing gates. When the N-floor const changes, it propagates to the tile automatically via the metrics-endpoint `pmf.killMinN` field — never reintroduce a client-side literal.

### depends_on ripple alert (locked 2026-05-13 — M-7 ship)

- **Closes the Aisha-persona blocker** surfaced in the 2026-05-12 audit (Section 8 A-2): "No proactive depends_on ripple alert when a structural assumption changes status." Until this ship, cross-decision detection only fired when the user opened the recommendations endpoint. The Cornerstone-magnetic moment — "the morning the WAEMU cycle assumption flips, see every dependent commit as a red banner" — required manual constellation navigation.
- **Architecture**: pure-function detector at [src/lib/containers/ripple-detection.ts](src/lib/containers/ripple-detection.ts) (`detectDependsOnRipples` + `groupRipplesByAnchor`). Read-only API at [/api/ripple-alerts](src/app/api/ripple-alerts/route.ts) (GET, 60s Cache-Control, scoped to user/org-visible containers + edges). UI banner at [RippleAlertBanner](src/components/dashboard/RippleAlertBanner.tsx) — mirrors AmbientSignalBanner's shape (polls 90s, self-hides when empty, caps at 3 grouped anchors, dismissals ride on sessionStorage). Mounted on /dashboard inside an ErrorBoundary directly below AmbientSignalBanner.
- **Trigger semantics (v1)**: HIGH severity fires when (a) anchor.status === 'archived', OR (b) anchor.outcome.brierScore ≥ 0.20, OR (c) anchor.outcome.summary contains failure-class language (`/failed|missed|did not achieve|below target|did not deliver|underperformed|destroyed value|wrote down|writedown|wrote off/i`). MEDIUM severity fires when anchor.outcome.brierScore ∈ [0.10, 0.20). Otherwise no ripple. Dependent containers must themselves be `active` (no point alerting a dependent that's already archived).
- **Pure-function discipline**: the detector takes a `Map<id, ContainerLite>` + `DependsOnEdge[]` + optional `dismissedIds: Set<string>`. NO I/O. NO LLM. NO Prisma. The API endpoint does data fetch + slices, then passes pure data in. 16-test vitest suite at [ripple-detection.test.ts](src/lib/containers/ripple-detection.test.ts) locks every trigger + filter + sort path.
- **Dismissal model (v1)**: client-side sessionStorage under `di-ripple-alerts-dismissed-v1`. The underlying anchor state doesn't change just because the user clicked dismiss — a dismissed ripple will re-appear on the next browser session if the assumption is still broken AND the dependent is still active. By design — "dismissed" means "acknowledged", not "resolved". Server-side dismissal would require a new Prisma model; deferred until the dismissal noise is real.
- **No Prisma migration needed** — every signal flows through the existing `DecisionContainer.status`, `DecisionContainerOutcome.brierScore`, `DecisionContainerOutcome.summary`, and `DecisionContainerLink.linkType === 'depends_on'` columns.
- **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new ripple triggers (e.g., anchor's structuralAssumptions audit flags a Critical change), extend `classifyAnchor` in `ripple-detection.ts` + add a new `RippleReason` value + add a new entry to `REASON_LABEL` in `RippleAlertBanner.tsx` + extend the test suite in lockstep. The pure-function shape keeps the rule additive.

### Ambient Drive file-body capture (locked 2026-05-15 — M-6 ship)

- **Closes the last unshipped M-\* item from the 2026-05-12 audit** + the asymmetric-pitch BAFTA risk: T2.2 ambient capture was Slack-full-content but Drive-metadata-only. ~60% of fractional-CSO + smaller-fund-GP HXC prospects live in Google Drive, not Slack — "ambient capture across your toolchain" was a procurement-grade falsehood at the cold-context door until this ship. The founder chose the deep ship (not the disclaimer fork) per the discovery-discipline lock.
- **Architecture**: `pollDriveInstallationForSignals` in [ambient-thesis-detection.ts](src/lib/integrations/ambient-thesis-detection.ts) now lists files modified in the last hour inside `monitoredFolders`, downloads each via the existing `downloadFileContent`, flattens via the existing `parseFile()`, classifies the text via the same deepseek-v4-flash `classifyTextForThesisFormation` the Slack path uses, and persists a signal at confidence ≥ `SIGNAL_BANNER_THRESHOLD`. New Drive helper [listRecentFilesInFolders](src/lib/integrations/google/drive.ts) does a scoped `files.list` (parent-in-monitoredFolders + `modifiedTime >` floor + not-trashed, single bounded page).
- **Does NOT touch `changesPageToken`** — that Changes-API cursor is owned by the document-creation flow in `/api/cron/google-drive-sync`. A second consumer advancing it would silently starve the other. The scoped `files.list` + `(source, sourceRef)` idempotency is the correct shape for a fire-and-forget hint feature; the 1-hour lookback mirrors the Slack pattern exactly.
- **`sourceRef` is the STABLE Google file id** (NOT `fileId:modifiedTime`) — matches the doc-creation flow's dedup shape and avoids duplicate-signal noise from non-substantive re-saves. A heavily-revised file that already produced a signal is intentionally not re-signalled; the 14-day expiry + user dismiss/confirm bound that edge for a hint feature. Inline comment in the poller warns future sessions not to "fix" this to `fileId:modifiedTime` without revisiting the cost/noise trade.
- **Pure-function-first discipline** (mirrors M-3 / M-7): `resolveDriveParseMimeType` (google-apps → export-target mime; lockstep with `downloadFileContent`'s googleTypes map) + `selectParsableDriveFiles` (parsable-filter + `DRIVE_MAX_FILES_PER_PASS=25` cap, order-preserving) are pure + unit-tested. 13-test suite at [ambient-thesis-detection.test.ts](src/lib/integrations/ambient-thesis-detection.test.ts). The I/O orchestration stays a thin wrapper; per-file try/catch (`log.warn`, not silent) so one bad file (too large / export failure / unparsable) can't poison the batch.
- **`pollAllAmbientSources` Drive `select` extended** with `refreshTokenEncrypted/Iv/Tag` so the poller can build the Drive client without an N+1 re-fetch — symmetrical with how the Slack path passes `teamId` for `resolveToken`.
- **Privacy posture unchanged + preserved**: default OFF (`GoogleDriveInstallation.ambientCaptureEnabled`), folder-scoped via `monitoredFolders`, excerpt capped at 500 chars by `persistAmbientSignal`, 14-day expiry. No raw file content persisted beyond the 500-char excerpt.
- **No Prisma migration** — every field exists (`AmbientThesisSignal`, `GoogleDriveInstallation.ambientCaptureEnabled/monitoredFolders/refreshToken*`). Lint baselines unchanged (silent-catches 175 — the new catches are `log.warn`, not silent; counts 77; canonical-imports clean).
- **Forward-looking rule**: when `parseFile()`'s supported MIME set changes, update `DRIVE_PARSABLE_MIME_TYPES` in lockstep (it is deliberately conservative + the per-file try/catch is the safety net). When `downloadFileContent`'s `googleTypes` export map changes, update `resolveDriveParseMimeType` in the same commit — the two MUST agree or a Google-native file is downloaded as one format and handed to `parseFile()` as another. Email ingestion (the 3rd `source`) follows the same shape when it lands: list → fetch → `parseFile` → classify → `persistAmbientSignal`, pure helpers extracted + tested, no Changes-cursor coupling.

### PMI signal auto-extraction (locked 2026-05-13 — M-3 ship)

- **Closes the Tier 2.2 deferred follow-up** ("IC-memo PMI signal auto-extraction via deepseek-v4-flash"). Manual entry on PmiTrackerTab stays canonical; this layer is a UX accelerator that surfaces SUGGESTIONS the user accepts / edits / rejects. Every accepted suggestion still routes through POST `/api/decisions/[id]/pmi-signals` so the audit log + idempotency + Brier-scoring stays intact.
- **Architecture**: pure extraction helper at [src/lib/pmi/extract-from-memo.ts](src/lib/pmi/extract-from-memo.ts) (`extractPmiSignalsFromMemo` + `parseExtractionResponse`). API endpoint at [/api/decisions/[id]/pmi-signals/extract](src/app/api/decisions/[id]/pmi-signals/extract/route.ts) (POST, 10/hr rate limit, acquisition-mode containers only, fail-soft to manual entry on any failure). Wired into [PmiTrackerTab](src/components/containers/PmiTrackerTab.tsx) as an "Auto-extract from IC memo" button + suggestion preview block above the existing manual-entry form.
- **Model**: `deepseek-v4-flash` via Vercel AI Gateway (MODEL_RECOMMENDATIONS export). ~$0.0002 per extraction; 12-second timeout; content capped at 6K chars. Document picking priority: ic_memo > synergy_model > integration_plan > most-recently-analyzed.
- **Output schema**: `ExtractedPmiSignal[]` with key + verbatim quote (≤300 chars; literal substring of the memo, NEVER fabricated) + plain-language proxy + horizonDays (90/180/365) + predictedConfidence (0-1) + rationale. Quote is the procurement-grade evidence anchor — if rejected the quote explains why; if accepted it carries the IC-memo claim string.
- **Defensive parsing**: `parseExtractionResponse` strips markdown code-fence noise, drops entries with invalid keys / missing quote+proxy / duplicates, clamps predictedConfidence to [0, 1], defaults invalid horizonDays to 180, returns empty array on any parse failure. 13-test vitest suite at [extract-from-memo.test.ts](src/lib/pmi/extract-from-memo.test.ts) locks every defensive branch.
- **Audit-log action**: new `PMI_SIGNAL_EXTRACT_ATTEMPTED` (separate from `PMI_SIGNAL_RECORDED` which fires on accept). Procurement readers can distinguish "system suggested" from "user committed".
- **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new PMI signal keys, update `PMI_SIGNAL_KEYS` in BOTH [/api/decisions/[id]/pmi-signals/route.ts](src/app/api/decisions/[id]/pmi-signals/route.ts) (canonical) AND [src/lib/pmi/extract-from-memo.ts](src/lib/pmi/extract-from-memo.ts) (extractor) in the same commit. The system prompt's signal list MUST mirror the canonical list — the prompt teaches the LLM what to extract, the parser enforces the type discipline.

### Interaction Matrix (locked 2026-05-13 — M-1 ship)

- **The pairwise interaction matrix is 22×22** (`src/lib/ontology/interaction-matrix.ts` `INTERACTION_MATRIX`). Extended from 20×20 on 2026-05-13 to close the silent moat hole that had been live for 13 days since the 2026-04-30 paper-application sprint added DI-B-021 (illusion_of_validity) + DI-B-022 (inside_view_dominance) to `BIAS_EDUCATION` without extending the matrix. Until M-1, `getInteractionWeight(IV, OC)` and 41 other new-bias pair lookups returned the neutral 1.0 fallback — silently losing compound-engine amplification on every memo that fired either new bias.
- **Weights anchored on CLAUDE.md paper-application locks**: "Coherent Confidence" toxic combo (DI-B-021): IV+OC=1.5, IV+CB=1.4, IV+HE=1.3, IV+AU=1.3. "Reference-Class Blindness" toxic combo (DI-B-022, canonical Kahneman & Lovallo 2003): ID+PF=1.6, ID+OC=1.5, ID+IV=1.4, ID+CB=1.3. All other new-bias interactions seeded from research-grounded reasoning (narrative coherence ↔ groupthink, selective perception, etc.). The full per-cell rationale lives inline in the matrix file as comments.
- **Methodology version bumped 2.2.0 → 2.4.0** (the "compound patterns supplied" stamp). New audits scored against the 22×22 matrix stamp 2.4.0; historical audits in the DB re-rendering after deployment also stamp 2.4.0 because the engine recomputes. The version-progression card on the DPR cover surfaces this transition; the dqi-distribution-check regression report captures the score-shift envelope. METHODOLOGY_VERSION_2_2_0 stays exported for back-compat.
- **`MATRIX_DIMENSION` + `MATRIX_BIAS_KEYS` exports** are the canonical lookup for any surface that needs the dimension or the bias key list — see [DecisionAlphaTab](src/components/founder-hub/DecisionAlphaTab.tsx) "compound scoring matrix" prose for the canonical consumption pattern. Never hardcode "20×20" or "22×22" — derive.
- **Forward-looking rule**: every new bias landing in BIAS_EDUCATION MUST extend the matrix in the same commit. The test `MATRIX_BIAS_KEYS is a superset of BIAS_EDUCATION keys` blocks the ship if not. The compound-engine `compound-engine.ts` consumer of `getInteractionWeight` (imported as `getMatrixWeight`) picks up the new weights automatically.
- **Cascade-completion — now genuinely COMPLETE (U-3.1 + U-3.1b shipped 2026-05-17, grep-proven; was falsely "COMPLETE" 2026-05-15 → corrected to PARTIAL by the 2026-05-17 nightly audit → actually closed same day)**: commit `f14c025e` + the 2026-05-15 batch closed the genuinely-derived set (layout.tsx JSON-LD · OnboardingTour · proof page+client · EnhancedEmptyState · GenomeMethodologyViz · CredibilityTrio · R2FDecompositionCard · AiVerifyMappingClient · compliance/page · category-pitch · product-overview · TaxonomyClient). The nightly audit then proved (via `rg '20×20|20x20'`) the prior "every surface derives" was **materially false** — present-tense product/teaching claims still hardcoded the stale matrix dimension in 4 founder-USED data files. **U-3.1 (2026-05-17) closed them**: `competitive-positioning.ts` (5 sites: INVESTOR_QA / MOAT_LAYERS / killer-response / capability strip / `MarketSize.label`), `positioning-frameworks.ts:404` (demo script — incl. `400`→`${MATRIX_COMBINATIONS}` = 484), `founder-school/lessons.ts` (6 lesson title/body sites + the `30+ taxonomy` / `20-bias taxonomy` / `17 regulatory frameworks` strings), `founder-school/visualizations.ts` (caption + 2 pipeline-detail rows). All now import `MATRIX_DIMENSION` from `@/lib/ontology/interaction-matrix` + `getAllRegisteredFrameworks` / `BIAS_EDUCATION` and **interpolate `${MATRIX}` / `${FRAMEWORK_COUNT}` / `${BIAS_COUNT}` — never literal**. The one genuinely-hazardous string (lesson 1468 carried a literal `` `${FRAMEWORKS.length}` `` meta-reference that teaches the derivation) was converted with a `` \`\${FRAMEWORKS.length}\` `` escape, tsc-verified. count-drift baseline ratcheted 77 → 76 (one fewer hardcoded literal). **U-3.1b** added the `checkLockedCountDrift` SEMANTIC check to [scripts/audit-platform.mjs](scripts/audit-platform.mjs) — it greps the founder-USED assert-the-count allowlist for `20×20`/`20x20`/`21×21`/`30+ (cognitive) bias(es)/taxonomy`/`Twenty biases plus`/`20-base` (the exact regex-blind class the count-drift lint cannot match: `×` is not whitespace; "cognitive" sits between number + "biases"), skipping comment/history/derivation lines. **Run against the fixed tree it returns ZERO** — that is the grep-before-assert proof that "COMPLETE" is true this time, and the structural guard that catches any future regression of this class. `education-room-data.ts` is deliberately NOT in the allowlist (it's a deprecation-TEACHING deck — its cards already derive `${BIAS_COUNT}` and quote "30+ cognitive biases" to drill the founder OFF it; flagging a corrective surface is the V-4.1 false-positive-cluster anti-pattern). Legitimate non-fixes (history-prose / canonical / methodology-version — do NOT re-flag, the SEMANTIC check skips them): `founder-context.ts` RECENTLY-SHIPPED / POLISH-LOG entries; `bias-education.ts` `DI-B-020` canonical ID; `interaction-matrix.ts:12` ("extended from 20×20" accurate history); `dqi.ts:436` methodology-version-chain JSDoc; the `// Derived —` / `the M-1 regression` rationale comments in the swept files. **Forward-looking discipline: never write "cascade COMPLETE" without a grep-before-assert that proves zero residual. The `checkLockedCountDrift` SEMANTIC check now mechanises that proof — `node scripts/audit-platform.mjs` returning zero `locked-count-drift` IS the grep-before-assert. A false "done" let the prior session skip the real work; the structural check makes that recurrence detectable at the discovery-tool layer.**

### Plan Limits & Billing

- Free tier: 4 analyses/month (defined in `src/lib/stripe.ts` → `PLANS.free.analysesPerMonth`)
- Limit enforced by `checkAnalysisLimit()` in `src/lib/utils/plan-limits.ts`
- Stripe price IDs may not be configured yet. Upgrade buttons must fall back gracefully to `/#pricing` when `PLANS.pro.priceId` is empty.
- **Admin full-access bypass.** Supabase user IDs listed in `ADMIN_USER_IDS` (Vercel env var, comma-separated) resolve to the `enterprise` plan in `getUserPlan()` / `getOrgPlan()` / `/api/billing` — no Stripe subscription needed. Intended for founder dogfooding and end-to-end testing. Bootstrap: set `ADMIN_EMAILS` first, deploy, visit `/api/admin/whoami` to discover your Supabase UUID, then paste into `ADMIN_USER_IDS` and redeploy. Helper: `isAdminUserId(userId)` in `src/lib/utils/admin.ts`.

### Team seat administration + audit trail (locked 2026-06-05 — Strategy 12-seat Tier A + B)

Refinement-grade hardening of the shipped Strategy (`$2,499/mo · 12 seats`, `PLANS.team.maxTeamMembers` in `stripe.ts`) tier. NO schema migration, NO speculative team features — the deeper team-only differentiators (Team DQI depth, Decision-Room voting upgrades) stay deferred per the GTM lock "team-tier feature set built FROM Sankore + Phase 1 feedback, NOT speculatively."

- **Seat enforcement is now two-sided.** Invite-time gating (`checkTeamSizeLimit`, members + pending invites) was the only check; accept-time was unguarded. [/api/team/invite/accept](src/app/api/team/invite/accept/route.ts) now resolves the org's CURRENT plan ceiling and does an **atomic member-count + insert inside one interactive `$transaction`** (`memberCount >= seatLimit → 403 SEAT_LIMIT_REACHED`). This closes (a) the count→insert race on two simultaneous accepts and (b) the **downgrade hole** — a stale invite created under Strategy can no longer push a since-downgraded org past its new cap. Deliberate: existing members are NEVER auto-removed on downgrade; growth is blocked, the over-limit state is surfaced, data is preserved.
- **Seat-usage meter.** `/api/team` GET now returns `seats: { plan, used, limit }` (authoritative, from `checkTeamSizeLimit`; `limit` = `Number.MAX_SAFE_INTEGER` for unlimited/Enterprise). TeamPage renders a `SeatMeter` (color-coded green/amber/red, over-limit honest copy) at the top of the Members tab + disables the Invite button when full. Client treats `limit > SEAT_UNLIMITED_THRESHOLD (100000)` as unlimited.
- **Team-admin audit trail.** 5 new `AuditAction` values (`TEAM_MEMBER_INVITED` / `_INVITE_REVOKED` / `_JOINED` / `_ROLE_CHANGED` / `_REMOVED`) wired into invite / accept / members(role+remove) / revoke. **`logAudit` gained an optional `orgId`** — set it on org-level actions so the row survives in the Team Activity feed + AdminAuditLog org filter even after the actor leaves. The Team Activity tab's `ACTION_LABELS` renders all 5.
- **Bulk invite.** New [/api/team/invite/bulk](src/app/api/team/invite/bulk/route.ts) POST `{ emails[], role }` — owner/admin-gated, 5/hr rate-limit, dedupes + normalizes, stops cleanly at seat headroom, returns per-email `{ created, skipped }` with reasons (`already_member` / `already_invited` / `seat_limit` / `invalid_email` / `self`). InviteModal gained a single ↔ multiple toggle (textarea, splits on whitespace/comma/semicolon).

**Forward-looking rules:** (1) every org-level `logAudit` call SHOULD pass `orgId` (the Team Activity + AdminAuditLog org filters depend on it). (2) any new path that creates a `TeamMember` MUST gate on the current-plan seat cap (members-only count) the way the accept route does — never trust the invite-time check alone. (3) the seat math lives in `checkTeamSizeLimit` (invite-time, pending-inclusive) + the inline accept-time member-count gate; don't add a third copy. (4) when the Strategy seat cap changes, edit `PLANS.team.maxTeamMembers` only — the meter + both gates read it; no hardcoded "12" in copy.

### Integrations

- **Slack:** 7 slash commands, thread monitoring, auto-creates CopilotSession + DecisionRoom after audits. Handler in `src/app/api/integrations/slack/events/route.ts`.
- **Google Drive:** OAuth + Changes API polling via cron. Dedup by `sourceRef` (Google file ID). Detects updated files by content hash comparison. 24h cooldown between re-analyses.
- **Email:** Unique address per user (`analyze+{token}@in.decision-intel.com`). Token-based auth.

## When to Push Back

Claude should push back on requests that:

1. **Add new top-level routes** — the sidebar already has 10 items and 25+ dashboard routes. Consolidate instead.
2. **Add features before the core flow is polished** — upload → analyze → review → track outcomes is the only flow that matters for pilot users.
3. **Skip error handling or schema drift protection** — every Prisma query in an API route needs a try-catch with P2021/P2022 fallback.
4. **Use hardcoded dark-mode colors** — always use CSS variables.
5. **Create duplicate utility functions** — check `src/lib/utils/` first. Especially `safe-compare.ts`, `cache.ts`, `rate-limit.ts`, `encryption.ts`.
6. **Make changes that break the build without testing** — run `npx tsc --noEmit` after significant changes.
7. **Add scope beyond what was asked** — the founder is in refinement phase. Don't add docstrings, comments, or refactoring that wasn't requested. **Exception**: when the request IS explicitly scoped as planned/Tier-N work (boil-the-ocean rule above), depth within the approved scope is required, not creep. The line is whether the deepening serves the approved item or wanders into adjacent surfaces.

## When to Ask Questions

Claude should ask the founder before:

1. **Creating new database models or fields** — schema changes require migrations and affect production.
2. **Modifying the analysis pipeline** (`src/lib/agents/`) — this is the core product. Even small changes can affect DQI scores across all users.
3. **Changing pricing, plan limits, or billing logic** — revenue-sensitive.
4. **Deleting any route or component** — may have external links, bookmarks, or Slack deep links pointing to it.
5. **Making changes visible to end users** (copy, labels, flow changes) — the founder has specific positioning and language preferences.

**Proactive-surfacing rule (locked 2026-05-09 evening — supersedes the default-skip pattern).** "Ask first" does NOT mean "default skip." When working on a non-trivial ship, Claude should ACTIVELY scan for high-leverage improvements in the pipeline / DQI / graph / Prisma / scoring engine that would deepen the build, then PROACTIVELY surface them to the founder with: (a) the specific change, (b) why it's high-leverage (load-bearing for what specifically — demo, procurement defensibility, future-proofing, etc.), (c) cost estimate (LOC + complexity), (d) risk assessment (what existing behaviour might shift), (e) clear recommendation. The founder decides; Claude then ships the deep version. Pre-shrinking by silently classifying improvements as "out of scope per the pipeline rule" burns the founder's leverage. The rule's true intent is "don't ship pipeline changes silently" — not "avoid pipeline work." Forward-looking: at the end of every multi-commit ship, run a brief "what did I deliberately skip touching the hard layers, and was that the right call" audit; surface the items where the answer is "no, this should ship." See "Velocity & Scope Discipline" lock above for the parent calibration.

## Build Hang Triage (READ THIS BEFORE TOUCHING THE BUILD)

Vercel build hangs cost ~$0 in money but ~45 minutes per attempt. The 2026-04-22 incident burned 11 hours and 30+ deploys because the right fix was found at hour 0, reverted at hour 1, then re-discovered at hour 11. Don't repeat that loop. The diagnostic chain below is the load-bearing artifact from that incident.

**Step 1 — locate the hang.** Pull the Vercel build logs and find the LAST log line before silence. Three known patterns:

| Last visible log line                                    | Cause                                                                                                                                                                                           | Fix                                                                                                |
| -------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `Successfully uploaded source maps to Sentry`            | [getsentry/sentry-javascript#17511](https://github.com/getsentry/sentry-javascript/issues/17511) — webpack plugin leaks undici sockets after upload, `runAfterProductionCompile` never resolves | `sourcemaps: { disable: true }` in `withSentryConfig` options. Already applied — do NOT revert it. |
| `Creating an optimized production build ...` (Turbopack) | Some Turbopack-only stall in this codebase. Not yet isolated.                                                                                                                                   | Stay on `next build --webpack`. The `--webpack` flag in `package.json:7` is load-bearing.          |
| `Creating an optimized production build ...` (webpack)   | Likely SWC infinite-loop on inline `<style>{`@media...`}</style>` blocks if `compiler.styledJsx: false` is missing                                                                              | Confirm `compiler: { styledJsx: false }` is in `next.config.ts`.                                   |

**Step 2 — reproduce locally before pushing any fix.** `npm run build` reproduces most build issues in 3-4 minutes. A failing local build is 10× cheaper to debug than a failing Vercel deploy. If it passes locally but fails on Vercel, the bug is environment-specific (network, container resource limits, Linux SWC binary differences) — and that itself narrows the search.

**Step 3 — bisect, don't theorize.** When N commits land between the last-green and the first-red, run `git bisect` against `npm run build`. The 2026-04-22 incident had 15 commits + ~5,000 LOC between green and red — bisection would have isolated the trigger in 4 build runs (~15 min) instead of 11 hours of theory-chasing.

**Things that have been ruled out as primary causes** (don't re-investigate without new evidence):

- Google Fonts fetch hang — fonts are now `@fontsource` local packages.
- `next/font/google` — removed.
- Turbopack font fetcher Rust HTTP path — fonts are local, the path doesn't fire.
- Sentry plugin telemetry — `telemetry: false` in `withSentryConfig`.
- Sentry source-map upload — DISABLED in `withSentryConfig`. **This is the load-bearing fix; do not revert.** Source maps will be uploaded post-deploy via the separate `npm run sentry:upload-sourcemaps` step (see Environment Variables → `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN`).
- Edge runtime on `app/opengraph-image.tsx` — file deleted; static OG image lives in `public/` instead.
- Heap exhaustion — `--max-old-space-size=7168` in NODE_OPTIONS gives webpack ~7 GB on Vercel's 8 GB build container; the pre-build tsc runs at `--max-old-space-size=3584` (~3.5 GB) in its own process, exits, then webpack starts.
- TypeScript errors — `npx tsc --noEmit` now runs clean; type-check phase no longer hangs silently on errors.
- **Stacked heap from two concurrent TS checks** (2026-04-23, deploy 4Sz9sqTpr, exit 137 after 6 min in "Running TypeScript..."). Next.js runs its own in-process TS check AFTER webpack compile finishes; combined with webpack's own heap it blew past 8 GB. Fix shipped: `typescript: { ignoreBuildErrors: true }` in next.config.ts, plus an explicit `NODE_OPTIONS='--max-old-space-size=3584' npx tsc --noEmit` step in the build script that runs **before** `next build`. The external tsc runs in its own process (~3 GB peak, then exits), then webpack runs at ~5 GB peak — never overlapping. Do NOT flip `ignoreBuildErrors` off without also removing the explicit tsc step, or type-checking gets silently skipped.
- **Webpack OOM at 6 GB heap** (2026-04-25, exit 137 during "Creating an optimized production build"). Codebase grew large enough that webpack's compile pass exceeded 6 GB even after the tsc step had freed its memory. Two-line fix shipped: (a) bumped webpack heap to 7168 (giving webpack ~7 GB on the 8 GB container, leaving ~1 GB for parent Node + container overhead) and dropped tsc heap to 3584 to phase the pressure cleanly, (b) enabled `experimental.webpackMemoryOptimizations: true` in next.config.ts — Next 16's built-in webpack memory optimization that drops a few non-essential webpack passes (unused-variable analysis tuning, some source-map auxiliary work) to keep peak memory under the 8 GB ceiling. No runtime impact; only changes how webpack does its bookkeeping during compile. Do NOT raise the heap above 7168 — that pushes the process into the parent-Node + container-overhead window and the SIGKILL fires.
- **Webpack OOM AGAIN at 7 GB heap** (2026-04-29, exit 137 during `next build --webpack` — even with `webpackMemoryOptimizations: true` already on). Codebase grew across the prior 7 days (Sparring Room v3 ~1700 lines, Education Room ~120 cards, Path-to-100M tab + ~3000-line data file, Closing Lab + Brinkmanship + Strategic Thinking sales-toolkit additions, founder-school lesson + visualization growth, the case-count drift refactor touching ~30 files). Fix: added `experimental.webpackBuildWorker: false` per the previously-documented next-OOM-move. Next 16+ runs webpack in a worker by default; disabling it can PARADOXICALLY reduce peak memory because the worker duplicates internal state that already lives in the parent process. **Did NOT switch to Turbopack** — per CLAUDE.md Build Hang Triage `--webpack` flag is load-bearing, and Turbopack stalled in this codebase on 2026-04-22 ("Creating an optimized production build ..." never recovered). Treat Turbopack as the experimental fallback ONLY if this commit's fix also OOMs. **If the 2026-04-29 fix also OOMs**, the next options are: (a) split heavy data files via dynamic import — best candidates: `src/lib/data/founder-school/lessons.ts` (~16K lines), `src/lib/data/founder-school/visualizations.ts` (~1300 lines), `src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data.ts` (~3000 lines), `src/components/founder-hub/education/education-room-data.ts` (~1700 lines) — wrap consumers in dynamic({ loading: ... }) so these don't hit the main bundle, (b) try Turbopack again if Next 16.x has improved the codebase compatibility (NB: this requires removing the `--webpack` flag from package.json :: scripts.build and likely fixing some inline-style edge cases SWC/Turbopack handles differently from webpack), (c) bump Vercel build-machine to a larger instance (Pro tier).
- **Webpack OOM (third) at 7 GB heap** (2026-05-06, exit 137 — even with all prior fixes already in place: heap 7168 + `webpackBuildWorker: false` + `webpackMemoryOptimizations: true`). Build log named the culprit explicitly — webpack's `PackFileCacheStrategy` was serialising 700+ MB cache packs (`.next/cache/webpack/server-production/1.pack` at 702 MB, `43.pack` at 428 MB, `index.pack` at 448 MB) and holding them in memory during serialisation, pushing peak heap past the 8 GB container ceiling. **Fix shipped**: added a `webpack(config, { dev })` callback in `next.config.ts` that sets `config.cache = false` for production builds. Vercel runs each deploy on a fresh container, so the on-disk cache hit rate is near-zero anyway — the disk packs were compute that never paid back. Trade-off: cold first-build locally on every restart (~3 min addition) but no impact on Vercel CI behaviour. Memory-cache alternative was rejected — webpack's memory cache also holds modules for the duration of the build, which at the codebase's current size also OOMs; only `cache: false` is stable. **If the 2026-05-06 fix also OOMs** (which would mean webpack's compile-only memory has crossed 7 GB without any cache contribution), the next options remain: (a) heavy-data-file dynamic-import splits per the 2026-04-29 list, (b) Turbopack retry, (c) Pro-tier larger build container.

**The load-bearing config — do not change without a passing build to prove the alternative works:**

- `package.json:7` build script: chain is `validate-deploy-env && prisma-migrate-safe && seed-business-data && tsc --noEmit && next build --webpack && upload-sourcemaps`. The external `tsc --noEmit` step is load-bearing per the 2026-04-23 stacked-heap fix. `seed-business-data.mjs` (added 2026-04-24) runs version-controlled pilot-data seeds (currently just Sankore) after migrations; it is create-only by default so UI edits to `founderNotes` are never clobbered, and it NEVER fails the build — DB-unreachable or seed-script errors log a warning and exit 0. Business data is not build-artifact-critical; the 11-hr build-hang postmortem's lesson is "don't let optional steps block the deploy."
- `next.config.ts` Sentry options: `sourcemaps: { disable: true }`
- `next.config.ts` compiler: `compiler: { styledJsx: false }`
- `next.config.ts` typescript: `{ ignoreBuildErrors: true }` — paired with the external tsc step above. Flip one, flip both.
- `NODE_OPTIONS='--max-old-space-size=7168'` on `next build`; `--max-old-space-size=6144` on the pre-build `tsc --noEmit` (webpack raised / tsc lowered to 3584 on 2026-04-25; **tsc raised 3584 → 6144 on 2026-06-14** after a real build OOM'd in the tsc step at ~3536 MB — "ineffective mark-compacts near heap limit" — the codebase's tsc working set had crept to the 3584 cap. Safe because tsc runs as its own process and fully exits before the webpack step (sequential `&&`), so peak memory is unchanged and any runner that can already run webpack@7168 has room for tsc@6144).
- `next.config.ts` `experimental.webpackMemoryOptimizations: true` (added 2026-04-25 alongside the heap rebalance — Next 16's built-in webpack memory optimization).

## Session Workflow

Claude Code sessions should follow this pattern for best results:

0. **Read TODO.md first.** Check `TODO.md` at the start of every session for known bugs, active priorities, and pending tasks. Update it as tasks are completed or new issues are discovered.
   0a. **Read the relevant md / architecture context BEFORE proposing or building — every session, every important suggestion (locked 2026-06-01, founder-directed).** CLAUDE.md + TODO.md are auto-loaded; actually USE them. Before suggesting _where_ something should live, confirm the surface's audience + access model. The recurring trap that prompted this rule: suggesting a personal Founder-Hub feature be surfaced on "the main dashboard." **`/dashboard` is the CUSTOMER product surface (upload → analyze → review, what paying CSOs see); `/dashboard/founder-hub` is the founder's PRIVATE, founder-pass-gated cockpit (Faith OS, Founder OS, Outreach ledger — single-user, founder-only data).** Never propose putting founder-only/personal surfaces on `/dashboard` or any customer-facing page; the Founder Hub IS the private home screen. Hold throwaway "future follow-up" lines to the same architectural rigor as the build itself — a careless suggestion that ignores the access model is a real error, not a small one. When in doubt about a surface's audience, grep the route group (`(marketing)` = public · `(platform)/dashboard` = customer · `(platform)/dashboard/founder-hub` = founder-private) before opening your mouth.
1. **Start small.** One focused task per session beats a mega-batch across 20 files. Context quality degrades past ~15 file modifications.
2. **Build-check before pushing.** Always run `npx tsc --noEmit` (fast, type-errors only) or `npm run build` (full build) before committing. The founder doesn't run builds locally — Claude IS the local build check.
3. **Commit after each logical unit.** Don't batch 12 changes into one commit. Ship fix → commit → next fix → commit.
4. **Don't rediscover — read CLAUDE.md.** The conventions here (CSS variables, `uploadedAt` not `createdAt`, `safeCompare` import) have all been learned the hard way.
5. **Pre-commit hook note:** There is a Gemini AI audit hook in `.husky/pre-commit` that runs `npm run audit:ai`. It can be slow. If it blocks and the changes are reviewed, use `--no-verify`.
6. **Keep CLAUDE.md current — proactively, not at session end.** Whenever a change introduces a new convention, renames a field, adds a critical file, changes a workflow pattern, or discovers a gotcha that cost time — update CLAUDE.md **in the same commit** as that change. Don't wait until the session ends. Don't ask permission. Just include the CLAUDE.md edit alongside the code change. Examples: adding a new Prisma field → update the Database section. Creating a new shared utility → add it to Key Files. Discovering a build error caused by a naming convention → add it to Critical Conventions. The goal is that the next session (which has zero memory of this one) starts with every lesson already learned.

## Debugging Discipline (locked 2026-04-22 after the 11-hour build-hang incident)

These five rules exist because the 2026-04-22 build-hang debug burned 11 hours and 30+ deploys re-discovering a fix that had already been found and wrongly reverted at hour 1. They are not optional.

1. **A working fix is not reverted without a NEW failing test that proves it wasn't the cause.** "It used to work without this" / "the old log shows this never fired" / "this can't be the cause because X" are guesses, not evidence. If a commit makes the build go green, the burden of proof is on the revert, not the keep. The 2026-04-22 incident's killer mistake was `c6af4ab` reverting `c1540a1`'s `sourcemaps: { disable: true }` on exactly this kind of "it used to work" reasoning.

2. **Bisect before theorize.** When N commits land between the last-green and the first-red, `git bisect run npm run build` is faster than any theory. Three builds (~12 min) beats three hours of reading code.

3. **Reproduce locally before pushing.** Each Vercel deploy attempt is 8-45 minutes. `npm run build` reproduces most issues in 3-4 minutes. Local first; push only after the local repro confirms the fix.

4. **Memory and commit messages record evidence + uncertainty, not conclusions.** Banned phrasings: "THE ACTUAL BUG", "definitively the culprit", "real root cause", "this is the fix". Every one of these in the 2026-04-22 commit history was followed by another red build. Use instead: "tried X, build now hangs at Y instead of Z" / "X eliminates the hang in deploy ABC123 — keeping unless disproved by a new failing case." The next session reads commit messages as ground truth — don't lie to it.

5. **Don't accumulate scaffolding without removing on disproof.** Each rejected hypothesis leaves debt: env vars, scripts, NODE_OPTIONS flags, config keys. When a hypothesis is disproved, delete its scaffolding in the same commit as the disproof, or document it as deliberately-kept-for-X with a date. The current build script still carries `patch-http-timeout.mjs` from a Google Fonts theory that's been irrelevant since fonts went local — don't let that pile grow.

## Sub-Agent Strategy

Use the right model for the right job. Never use Opus for tasks Haiku can handle.

**Exploration (Haiku, 3 in parallel):**
Use Haiku sub-agents for all read-only codebase exploration — file reading, grep searches, structure mapping, "find all places X is used" pattern analysis. Haiku reads files and reports back just as accurately as Opus. Launch up to 3 in parallel for maximum speed. Always specify `model: "haiku"` and `subagent_type: "Explore"` for these.

**Planning (Opus, main thread):**
Do implementation planning in the main conversation thread, not in sub-agents. The main thread has the full conversation context, user intent, and prior decisions. Delegating planning to a sub-agent loses this context and produces generic results. The one exception: use a Plan sub-agent (Opus) for very complex multi-file architectural decisions where a fresh perspective helps.

**Implementation (Opus, main thread, direct edits):**
Never delegate code implementation to sub-agents. Always edit files directly in the main thread. The main thread has the conversation history, knows what was tried, and can make judgment calls. Sub-agents writing code produce lower-quality output because they lack this context.

**Verification (Sonnet or direct Bash):**
For mechanical checks — type-checking, test runs, build verification, counting occurrences — use direct Bash commands (preferred) or Sonnet sub-agents if parallel checking is needed. These tasks don't need Opus-level reasoning.
